Lord Martanos
was a
paladin
and a captain in the
Zakarum
during the
Zakarum Crusade
.
Biography
A once-noble holy warrior of
Zakarum
, Martanos fell to hatred during
a campaign
to conquer
Ivgorod
in
Rakkis
's name. While many of the Zakarum faithful were suborned by
demons
, Martanos's zeal and desire to convert unbelievers saw his aims align naturally with
Mephisto
— and his
soul
slip into damnation with ease.
Zakarum Crusade
"I am the hand of the
Zakarum
, and I will tear the heresy from you"
- Martanos to a defeated
Sladyan
(
src
)
Lord Martanos mobilizing Zakarum soldiers
Lord Martanos was the leader of the
Brotherhood of Light
—a regiment sect of the Zakarum.
During the
Zakarum Crusade
, he was tasked with purging
Zavain
of heretics. His army murdered and pillaged
their way through the mountain, with
the Veradani monastery
being the final obstacle. He slaughtered the
monks
there without mercy.
A tainted Martanos battling Sladyan
By an unknown means, he gained a
demonic
taint for more power. He was able to easily overpower
the patriarch
of the monastery but was trapped on an isolated peak. He perished with the remaining invading force and the monks by the
mist
that was released by the
Ancient Nightmare
.
His body was recovered and buried in the
Zakarum Cemetery
at Mount Zavain.
Undeath
"This land... belongs to Zakarum... and yet you have loosened your grip upon it. This is weakness... the deeds of an unbeliever... a recreant!"
- Lord Martanos' spirit
(
src
)
Martanos rises from his grave
Martanos' hatred borne from zealotry ensured his spirit was unable to move on, and his hatred contributed to the darkness that tainted the region.
Two centuries later
, his spirit was roused when
a young Rakkisguard
attempted to purify the darkness.
In time, he was able to resurrect as a
skeleton
, but was later killed by
the Shard-seeker
(s).
In-game
Undead Lord Martanos is a world boss that can be seen at
his grave
in Mount Zavain. An alive Martanos is seen as a mini-boss in the quest,
Forgotten Nightmares
.
Combat
Martanos fights using a flail and a tower shield. He can also
throw his shield
and
desecrate
an area to
slow
and
damage
an enemy. At the latter part of the battle, the undead Martanos summons
his
soldiers
to fight for him.
History
A boss spawn indicator was added in the
April 29, 2025
update.
Trivia
Martanos' corruption likely originated from his left pauldron which was
cursed
. Originally, it had a dark blue miasma. After it started twisting his flesh, it gained a rocky appearance similar to partly cooled magma and spikes started growing from it. After he resurrected, it lost its magma-like appearance, but remained spiked.

PAGE: Lord Wynton
CATEGORIES: Characters
URL: https://diablo.fandom.com/wiki/Lord_Wynton
======================================================================

Wynton
Title
The Usurper
Gender
Male
Race
Human
Affiliation
Westmarch
Occupation
Noble
Relatives
Rakkis
,
Korsikk
(ancestors)
Korelan
(great grandfather)
Status
Deceased
Appearances
Diablo Immortal
(mentioned only)
Diablo III: Reaper of Souls
Lord Wynton
was a noble of
Westmarch
who used the chaos of Malthael and the Reapers' assault on the city to try to seize Westmarch's throne. He has
a market
in
Rakkis Plaza
.
Biography
Wynton claims his grandmother was the daughter of
Korelan
, making him a rightful heir to the throne (even though she was born from a courtesan, not a queen). He spent years conspiring against
King Justinian IV
, and his disagreements with the crown were known. Lord Wynton used the peasants' growing displeasure towards the royalty to weaken the king's rule.
During the
Reapers
' assault on
Westmarch
, Justinian believed that Wynton would aid in the crisis. Instead, Wynton inspired peasants to slaughter a number of nobles supporting the crown, took the whole regiment of soldiers and killed the king, with the intention of bringing the
Rakkis
bloodline back onto the throne of
Westmarch
and consolidating his rule by killing all who opposed him. Outraged by Wynton's actions and their worsening of an already horrific situation,
the Nephalem
slew Wynton shortly after.
In-game
Diablo Immortal
Though he doesn't appear in-game, Wynton is implied to be the owner of
Wynton's Grand Market
.
Diablo III
Lord Wynton in Clyfton Hall
Wynton is a
Super Unique
enemy found during "
The True Son of the Wolf
"
event
in
Clyfton Hall
at
Westmarch Heights
. His in-game physique is larger than that of any other
human
character in the game. 
Initially, upon entering the throne room, players are not engaged in combat with Lord Wynton. Speaking with him, however, starts the battle. He leads off the battle by saying that he has spent his whole life preparing for this day, and usually calls the player by their class, with the exception of the
Witch Doctor
, whom he calls a "primitive heathen".
Lord Wynton carries the
Defender of Westmarch
shield
and a
sword
very similar to
Exarian
. He has the Knockback and Extra Health affixes in combat, and in addition the following abilities:
Skull Cracker
: a melee blow that inflicts
Knockback
to the target.
Charge
: A long-range rush that deals damage and a 2 second
Stun
, similar to
Kormac's
ability of the same name.
He is assisted by rebel
Westmarch Soldiers
(archers and shieldguard), as well as two
Vizjerei
Hired Mages
. The latter do not fight, but instead channel a shield that makes Lord Wynton completely immune to damage as long as at least one Mage is alive. Every 30 seconds, or every 25% of his
Life
, Lord Wynton can summon a new pair of mages, while soldiers arrive every few seconds. The Nephalem may not retreat from combat (as the door locks behind them when the battle starts), but being killed does not reset the event.
Unique
Inquisitors
use his model.
Media
Diablo 3 Reaper of Souls Killing Lord Wynton
Lord Wynton in combat

PAGE: Lord of Goats

"
Maghda
is a fool. I will raise an army of
souls
from
these primitives
and chain them to my invincible will. Yes, with these heathens at my command, the kingdoms of the world shall bow to the might of... The Lord of Goats! I may have to work on the title a bit more."

)
The
Lord of Goats
is a minor character in
Act I
of
Diablo III
.
He is always found in
Southern Highlands
(only in
Campaign Mode
), at the same location (a small ridge in the easter part of the map), chanting over the four Kharza mummies. When approached, he will exclaim that the player is doomed, and then raise four ghostly
Khazra Brutes
to aid him in combat.
Lord of Goats himself is an ordinary Dark Cultist with no extra abilities. Upon death, he drops
A Summoner's Journal
, revealing that he had a plan to conquer the world with an army of invincible
undead
goatmen. While in game he is named only "Dark Cultist", the Lord of Goats is his self-proclaimed title.

for "protection," which resulted in Meros's gemstone cache being taken by Luskas as 'payment.' Meros sent
the Wanderer
to retrieve the gemstones. Luskas was killed, and the gemstones returned.
In-game
Luskas is encountered in the
side quest
"
Gold Well Spent
." He attacks via melee, and is encountered alone.
Quotes

Luzja
Gender

(mother)

Diablo Immortal
Luzja
was the daughter of
Aisah
.
Biography
While on
Mount Zavain
, Aisah was supposedly abducted by the
Cult of Damnation
. Luzja found herself surrounded by
khazra
, but she was saved by
Caulder
and an
adventurer
. Caulder sent the adventurer after the cult while he stayed with Luzja. The adventurer returned with Aisah's lyre, and believing that Aisah would find them when she heard it, she began to play. What the adventurer didn't tell Luzja was that her mother was actually a member of the cult, and had planned on sacrificing her daughter.
Caulder agreed to take Luzja back to
Sentinel's Watch
, and hopefully send her to
Westmarch
in turn, as she'd have a better chance than in the wilderness. The two headed back, and Caulder told Luzja that her music was beautiful. Luzja asked Caulder if she knew where her mother was, to which he uneasily responded that he was sure she was on her way back.
In-game
Luzja appears as an
NPC
in
Diablo Immortal
. She features in the
side quest
"
The Bond
."

"There are many ways to open a door. I happen to know most of them."
- Lyndon
(src)
Lyndon
Title
The Scoundrel
Gender
Male
Race
Human
Affiliation
Thieves Guild
(formerly)
The Nephalem
(formerly)
Disciples of Sanctuary
(formerly)
Backwater
Class
Scoundrel
Occupation
Thief, con artist, etc.
Town boss
Relatives
Edlin
(brother),
Rea
(sister-in-law), unnamed nieces and/or nephews
Status
Active
Appearances
Diablo III
Diablo III: Reaper of Souls
Diablo IV
Diablo IV: Lord of Hatred
(mentioned only)
Lyndon the Scoundrel
is one of the three
Followers
featured in
Diablo III
and a NPC quest giver in
Diablo IV
.
Biography
Early Life
"My brother taught me when we were younger. He thought the crossbow was the best weapon for me since it would give me time to run away if I botched things too badly."
"Where is he now?"
"Oh, he's still in Kingsport. I expect he'll be there a good long time."
- Lyndon and the Nephalem
(
src
)
Lyndon, and his brother
Edlin
, grew up orphans in the slums of
Kingsport
.
His brother taught him how to fight and how to use a
crossbow
, reasoning that it would give Lyndon time to run if things went awry.
Lyndon
As Lyndon grew older he developed a skill for theft and joined the
Thieves Guild
against Edlin's advice,
while his brother became a member of the
city guard
.
Lyndon fell in love with a woman named
Rea
, but his feelings were not reciprocated, and she ultimately chose to marry his brother instead.
As a member of the Thieves Guild, Lyndon was privy to all of their plans, and contrived a scheme to work with Edlin to their advantage. Lyndon would tip him off to the Guild's targets, while Edlin would bring the guards on to the scene of the crime, and play it off like a lucky catch. When Lyndon's crew robbed the
Merchants Guild Bank
however, Edlin showed up too early and was accused of being involved in the heist. Edlin was confined to Kingsport's prison, while Lyndon managed to escape and flee the city.
Ever since, Rea believed Lyndon was responsible for Edlin's imprisonment, and eventually convinced Edlin of the same.
On the Road
"What do you do with all of the riches you find?"
"Living a life of depravity and overindulgence, naturally."
"In this cold and desolate place? I doubt it."
"Fine. Perhaps I have found that my treasure is put to better use elsewhere."
- The Nephalem and Lyndon
(
src
)
Lyndon
In the years prior to the coming of the
Fallen Star
, Lyndon spent his time moving from place to place to escape the Thieves Guild's wrath, conning locals, seducing ladies, and relieving the unwitting of their drink and money in order to help provide for Edlin's family and pay off his 'debts' to the
Merchants Guild
.
The threat of imprisonment or from armed guard has never dissuaded Lyndon from living a life of larceny as he journeyed the land.
For all the
gold
he sent to Rea in order to pay off Edlin's debt, he received no word in response.
At some point, he knew a woman from Caldeum, but he left her. While he described her as being "fair as the sun," he also reasoned,  "every sun must set."
The End of Days
In
1285
, Lyndon was in
Khanduras
. He discovered that a family near
New Tristram
had obtained a valuable relic. He decided to get it by going through their daughter,
Sasha
.
He was able to successfully woo her.
At
The Old Mill
, Lyndon encountered
The Nephalem
en route
to the
Drowned Temple
. He convinced the hero to help aid him in saving Sasha from the Thieves Guild brigands. After dispatching the brigands, he retrieved his relic from Sasha and hastily concocted a excuse to escape his 'betrothal' by accompanying The Nephalem's group. His efforts, however, were in vain - the relic was a fake. He subsequently offered his services to The Nephalem and accompanied the hero(es) on their journey to the Temple.
Lyndon stuck with the Nephalem as they traveled to
Kehjistan
,
Bastion's Keep
, and into the
High Heavens
in order to thwart
Diablo
.
With
Adria
's betrayal, he fell into despair.
After the final battle with the Prime Evil, the Nephalem suspected the presence of tears in the scoundrel's eyes who assured the Nephalem that it was raining. Towards the end of the quest, the Nephalem gifted Lyndon with gold, declaring that they would travel to Kingsport and pay off Edlin's debt once the quest was over. Lyndon was overwhelmed with gratitude.
Reaper of Souls
During
Malthael
's invasion, Lyndon finally decided he had to free Edlin from the Kingsport dungeons before he died there. After hearing from a
Westmarch
Dungeon Guard that prisoners from Kingsport had been transferred to
Westmarch
, he and the Nephalem proceeded to the dungeons in hopes of freeing Edlin.
Upon their arrival, the pair realized that the Thieves Guild had managed to infiltrate the dungeon. After fighting their way through the complex, Lyndon entered his brother's cell, only to discover that Edlin had been murdered. A wave of remorse and grief swept over Lyndon as he bitterly blamed himself for the death of his brother. Upon inspection of Edlin's body, he took the dagger that was used to kill him, and noted how suspiciously familiar it was.
The Nephalem attempted to console Lyndon, but was rebuffed, Lydon said that the great hero could never understand his grief. Despondent and mournful, Lyndon indulged in a drunken binge. The Nephalem eventually confronted him, and offered to help find Edlin's killer, but Lyndon ignored the offer and continued in an intoxicated state.
Later, however, he left the dagger he found with
Haedrig Eamon
, and the Nephalem asked him to tell them more about it. After remarking on the craftsmanship of the dagger, Haedrig noticed that the hilt was hollow, inside which was a note. The Nephalem gave the note to Lyndon. It appeared that Rea, Edlin's wife, had murdered him. The note said that if Lyndon wanted to seek revenge, she would be waiting for him. Lyndon resolved to find Rea after Malthael was dealt with.
Disciples of Sanctuary
Having long been in study and observation of The Nephalem,
Kormac
,
Eirena
, and Lyndon formed the
Disciples of Sanctuary
, continuing to fight against the minions of Hell.
Backwater
"Boss runs a tight ship around here."
"Ugh, too tight, you ask me. I came here to escape tyranny, now I'm stuck lickin' a tyrant's boots."
"Shut yer trap! He's got goons everywhere. Talk like that, you'll find yourself short a few fingers."
-
Teodar
,
Antal
, and
Rodney
(
src
)
During the
Great Enmity
, Lyndon became boss of
Backwater
; a
town
on the coast of
Hawezar
. He ran a tight ship, where just speaking out against him could cost his underlings a few fingers.
While boss of Backwater, Lyndon played a game of
Skull & Anchor
where according to rumor, he won the
leathers
of his opponent. He apparently gave the leathers back, as he wanted to give the poor sod something warm without wounding his pride.
After the supposed return of
Akarat
, numerous pilgrims flocked to Backwater to follow their prophet to
Skovos
. Lyndon handed numerous bags (implied to be currency) to the pilgrims.
This section is a
stub
. You can help the Diablo Wiki to become more awesome by
expanding it
.
In-game
Diablo III
Lyndon is first met at
The Old Mill
in
Act I
, while on the way to the
Drowned Temple
with
Leah
. He is voiced by
Troy Baker
.
[[File:|thumb|Lyndon in Backwater, Hawezar]]
Equipment
Lyndon's armor progression
Lyndon fights with ranged weapons, specifically bows,  allowing him to keep his distance from the enemy. In battle, he fires quick bolts or arrows at enemies to cripple them, stun them, or do moderate single-target damage. Lyndon also carries pieces of unique equipment with him; mementos of a life guided by wit and luck, such as loaded dice, razors, or mysterious pouches. These souvenirs, known as Scoundrel Tokens, improve his ability in combat as much as, if not more than, the jewelry and other trinkets he collects.
The Scoundrel has the highest damage output of all the followers. When fitted with high dexterity, damage, and critical gear, he can do almost as much damage as the player.
Available equipment:
Amulets
Rings
Bows
Crossbows
Scoundrel Tokens
(special item)
Skills
Lyndon's skills increase your party’s damage, as well as his own ability to cripple or poison opponents and his capacity to evade attacks. He can also gain the ability to strike multiple foes at once with a salvo of arrows or a carefully placed explosive bolt.

Personality and Traits
"And that Lyndon. Ha! He makes me laugh. He can warm my bed any night. Reminds me of my second husband, he does."
-
Myriam Jahzia
(
src
)
Lyndon
"Rogue" and "rake" are two words that describe Lyndon. Outwardly, he appears charming and unhesitatingly selfish, lusting after women, wine, and wealth. Inwardly, he was dedicated to the fight against
demons
and other monsters,
and was wracked with guilt over his brother's predicament.
He has a tendency to exaggerate the charms of Kingsport.
Lyndon is, as suggested, an incredibly good thief; deft and subtle enough to steal
Leah
's
ring
from her finger without her even noticing (though
The Nephalem
did see that act easily).
He is also skilled at dice.
In his twilight years, Lyndon displayed a ruthless streak when it came to running Backwater, but was not above acts of charity either.

Gossip about Lysander
Some of the other locals give their thoughts concerning Lysander.
Atma
Oh, Lysander is cranky, but he's a good old man. He used to give me medicines when... my son was ill.
Drognan
Lysander is harmless enough. We keep each other company with our mutual interests, yet I don't think he could handle the enormity of our present situation.
Elzix
That Lysander's a grumpy old cuss. You'd better not disturb him while he's working on his potions, or... BOOM! You could get blasted to the moon.
Geglash
I've got no time for old alchemists. Lysander would be completely useless in a real fight.
Greiz
I'd stay clear of Lysander, if I were you. He's always mixing his damned potions and chemicals. I wouldn't be surprised if he winds up blowing himself to smithereens!
Jerhyn
For trade in magic and the like, see Drognan or Lysander. Drognan is the wisest man I know - without equal in magic and ancient lore. Poor Lysander is nearly deaf, but he's a reliable potion chemist.

"Looking for something?"
"An axe. Specifically the axe of "the woodsman", a man who stalked and butchered travelers in this area. Rumor has it that the woodsman disappeared recently and left his weapon behind. The priest who hired me didn't offer much more to go on. At this rate I'll freeze before I find the damn thing. If you help me find the axe, I'll cut you in on the pay. Check the woods around town. I'm staying here where it's safe."

and Magdalena
(
src
)
Magdalena
Gender
Female
Race
(
Undead
)
human
Affiliation
Cathedral of Light
(temporary)
Occupation
Treasure hunter
Status
Deceased
Appearances
Diablo IV
Magdalena
was a treasure hunter/finder.
Biography
" Magdalena has been in my employ for years, it pains me greatly to know what has happened. If such an artifact was found in Nevesk, I will see that town burned to the ground and the earth salted. Who knows what other foul things slithered out of that town?"
- Parin
(
src
)
Magdalena did various jobs for
Parin
; a priest of the
Cathedral of Light
. She procured numerous odd items or objects with a history for him. He paid well for them, but she didn't know what he wanted them for.
In
1336
, Parin requested Magdalena retrieve
the Woodsman's Axe
. Parin didn't offer her much to go on, only that it had belonged to a
murderous individual
who had killed numerous people around
Nevesk
, and that the individual had recently disappeared. Magdalena arrived in Nevesk, but made no headway. She was approached by
the Wanderer
, and offered them a share of the profit if they found the axe for them. The Wanderer returned with the axe, and Magdalena was glad to leave, as she couldn't shake the feeling she was being watched. She headed to
Menestad
to collect her due.
Somewhere along the way to Menestad, Magdalena apparently succumbed to the axe's baleful influence. When she arrived, Parin and a retinue of
Knights Penitent
were looking for her, but with a pained expression, apparently unable to stop herself, she attacked them, cutting down the knights as if they were children. Still with the axe, she fled into a
nearby cellar
, where she was confronted by the Wanderer and killed.
Her
soul
was apparently consumed by the axe, as later, when it was being destroyed by holy water, she manifested in spirit form to attack the Wanderer, but was put down once more. Parin stated that he didn't know what became of the souls of the axe's victims, but could only hope that they found the
Light
.
In-game
Magdalena in spirit form
Magdalena appears as an
NPC
in
Diablo IV
. She is located in Nevesk. Talking to her initiates the "
The Woodsman of Nevesk
"
side quest
.
Magdalena is later encountered as a
monster
in "
Chain of Possession
" and "
Legacy Unmade
." She attacks via melee.

Biography
"Another of the Magistrate's victims? You certainly fit the profile he preys upon."
"What's happening here?"
Came looking for the Magistrate, too. These vampiric cult members conceal themselves in more places than you'd imagine."
-
Erys
and
the Wanderer
(
src
)
In
1336
, Oren's town was plagued by
vampires
.
Rumors of missing merchants swirled around town.
In truth, Oren was in league with them. Dozens of victims were lured into his
office
, and a number of
adventurers
were caught in his web, in order to be transformed into
Blood Seekers
. However, his master, Lord
Zir
, was not satisfied with his efforts.
Still playing the role of a concerned magistrate, Oren requested aid from
the Wanderer
to investigate the recent slew of murders.
Upon their arrival, Oren directed them to investigate
Vasily's Reach
in
Scosglen
, where the last caravan had gone missing.
After their departure, Oren was summoned by Zir to the
Tomb of Hallows
. A retinue of vampires was left in his office to ambush anyone who came to investigate.
Oren expected to be rewarded for his efforts.
Entering the tomb however, he was surrounded by a group of vampires.  He begged for mercy, but was executed.
Erys
later theorized that Zir was aware that she and the Wanderer had complicated things, and that Oren had been killed because of Zir's frustration and/or to prevent him from giving them information.
In-game
Oren appears in Ked Bardu in
Season of Blood
. He plays a role in the introductory "
Blood Money
"
quest
, and is seen again briefly in "
Summons of the Deathless
." His
ring
is obtained along the season questline.

Gender

Diablo III
Marta
was the wife of
Rondal
. They met (and possibly married) in
1241
. Marta noted that Rondal often stated that he might not come back from the field, despite beating the odds every time.
At some point, Marta gifted Rondal with a
locket
.
In
1255
, Marta was kidnapped by
Barbarians
in an ambush, but they returned her two hours later with an apology. Marta later commented that she simply reasoned them. Years on,
Garma
still sent her hides by way of apology.
In
1285
, they were at
Bastion's Keep
when it came under siege by
Azmodan
. As per usual, Rondal warned his wife that he might not return from the field. Marta commented that he'd been saying that for 44 years.
They were still in the keep's
stronghold
when
demons
emerged from below. Fortunately, they were repelled by
The Nephalem
. Rondal joked that he'd ask if Marta was alright, but that he knew better.
The Nephalem was able to drive the demons from the keep itself, though the siege continued. Rondal commented that things were looking up. He was reluctant to take too much credit, as he pointed out there were other soldiers, but Marta stated that she hadn't noticed.
She stated that thanks to The Nephalem's efforts, he could get some rest (despite Rondal's protestations that he felt fine). When word reached them that The Nephalem had defeated
Azmodan
, they planned to leave the keep. This didn't come to pass however, as
Adria
turned on the keep's defenders, killing Rondal among numerous others. Marta was consumed by grief, and refused comfort from The Nephalem.

PAGE: Maurice
CATEGORIES: Characters
URL: https://diablo.fandom.com/wiki/Maurice
======================================================================

Maurice
Gender
Male
Race
Human
Affiliation
Westmarch
House Natoli
Occupation
Soldier (formerly)
Servant
Status
Active
Appearances
Turn of a Card
Maurice
is a servant of
House Natoli
.
Biography
At some point, Maurice served as a soldier. In his aged later years, he acted as a servant for
House Natoli
. When
Ashton Natoli
disappeared, and
Nerissa Natoli
was left with his debts and a diminishing household, Maurice remained loyal to the family. A year after Ashton's disappearence, he arrived back home, in the form of a delivered corpse. It was in the midst of this that he observed his mistress playing card games with
Carlotta
, a woman who, despite her apparent age, could move much faster than he could. After the second visit, Nerissa requested Maurice fetch her an oil lamp, as she began writing to the creditors, begging for more time. As he returned, finding
Elizabeth
with her sister, Elizabeth suddenly span round, knocking the lamp out of Maurice's hands. Elizabeth's hair caught fire, and she was severely disfigured by the blaze. Maurice was sent out to find the healers, and while they saved her life, they could not save Elizabeth's visage. Maurice blamed himself for the accident, despite Nerissa insisting that he wasn't to blame. He stood on watch like a soldier for Carlotta, who sure enough, arrived a third time. Carlotta strode past him, and he announced Carlotta's presence to his mistress after she had done so herself. Nerissa let him leave as they began their third and final card game.
References

======================================================================
PAGE: McMahon
CATEGORIES: Characters
URL: https://diablo.fandom.com/wiki/McMahon
======================================================================

McMahon
Title
First mate
Gender
Male
Affiliation
Captain
Hanso
Status
Deceased
McMahon
was the first mate to Captain
Hanso
.
Biography
At some point after the
Mage Clan Wars
, McMahon and co. sailed north-east from
Kingsport
on a mining expedition. He made a
log
of his experiences. From the outset, he was disgruntled, as while he'd expected the position of first mate to be exciting, all he did initially was watch the deckhands argue. To make matters worse, he became seasick, but repeatedly refused Hanso's offers of ale to alleviate his symptoms.
At some point, the ship was caught in a storm. After being battered for three days, a tidal wave carried them inland into
Kehjistan
, stranding them in the desert. Hanso disappeared soon after landfall, and the surviving crewmembers were convinced that some sort of monster was after them. McMahon wondered if the survivors were the unlucky ones.
The crew's fears turned out to be accurate, and the creatures attacked the wreck while the crew was sleeping. McMahon managed to get away, but he doubted he would last long. He could hear the creatures in the shadows...giggling...

(master)
Occupation
Artist
Relatives
Unnamed parents
Status
Unknown
Appearances
Diablo Immortal
(mentioned only)
Miray
was the apprentice of
Vithu
.
Biography
At some point, Miray imagined the
Void
, and drew it for her parents.
Apparently, like Vithu, her painting of the Void drove her parents to commit suicide, as they chased the sublimity of their feelings.
While technically guilty of causing the
deaths
of her parents, she blamed the Void.
At some point after her parents' deaths, Miray approached Vithu. To the seer's surprise, she begged to be his apprentice.
Vithu accepted Miray's apprenticeship, and they painted the Void in new colors, undeniable, but robbed of all its power.
She eventually eclipsed her mentor's talent, which.
She returned home one night to find him gone, and perfectly oval holes cut through the roof and floor of her home.
In-game
Miray is mentioned in
Diablo Immortal
in the text flavor of
Vithu's Urges
item set
.

======================================================================
PAGE: Mishka
CATEGORIES: Characters
URL: https://diablo.fandom.com/wiki/Mishka
======================================================================

Mishka
Gender
Male
Race
Human
Status
Active
Appearances
Unyielding
Mishka
is a young boy, currently under the protection of
Zhota
.
Mishka's hair is long, almost transluscent. He has a thin mousy face, and his skin is extremely pale. Blind, his eyes are stark white, and
weep blood
(something that he can't control). Red veins are visible all around them, as if his face has been slashed numerous times. His stamina is poor.
Biography
Miskha was born c.
1275
; the son of a
Patriarch
and a concubine. He was born with deformities, but his mother convinced his father to sequester him in the
Floating Sky Monastery
rather than killing him. His mother would often play
The Trickster of the Moss Barrows
for him. She also told him that those who claimed he was cursed for weeping blood were fools.
Mishka lived in isolation until the coming of the
Fallen Star
, causing paronoia to sweep
Ivgorod
. Apparently, Mishka's father ordered that his son be put to death, lest his purity be called into question. Thus, through the work of his mother and a few loyal servants, Mishka was carried into the
Gorgorra
. However, the caravan was attacked. Mishka's mother told him to flee, telling him that she would play a song on her flute when it was safe. Days passed, and he heard no sound. In truth, his mother and the servants were dead.
Zhota came across the
bloody
scene, and picked up Mishka's flute. Playing a few notes, Mishka reacted in the nearby bushes, catching Zhota's attention. Zhota easily caught him. Zhota purified the bodies of the fallen, and Mishka remained silent for the next few days, though one night, whispered "mother" in his sleep. He tried to escape on several occassions, but Zhota bound his hands. Mishka's slow pace slowed Zhota's progress to a crawl, and he began taunting the boy, calling him "
demon
child." Eventually, Mishka exclaimed that he wasn't a demon. He further claimed that he couldn't trust Zhota, as he'd "played the wrong song." Zhota told Mishka that he wasn't responsible for his mother's death. Mishka wasn't put at ease however, as he believed that the demon that had killed his mother was still out there.
After five days of travelling, and passing through numerous empty villages, the pair finally exchanged their names. Mishka also began to play
Trickster
, much to Zhota's annoyance. Nevertheless, Zhota's demenour had softened towards the boy, and had begun to carry him for periods of time. That night, they were confronted by a group of brigands. They claimed that the Patriarchs had hired their services in lending aid to the people of the Gorgorra. Specifically, one of Zhota's fellow Monks had told them of a demon that wore the face of a blind child, and had "hair as white as snow." Mishka cried, claiming that he wasn't a demon, but his tears of blood were all the proof that the brigands needed that he was cursed, if not outright demonic. Zhota told the men that he would see the Monk that had entrusted them to this task, and refused to pay them anything. This led to blows, but Zhota easily defeated the brigands. He demanded to know why a demon was after Mishka. The boy explained that his father had sent it, and told Zhota the story of his origins.
The next day, Zhota found the Monk the brigands were referring to—
Akyev
, who likewise maintained that Mishka was a demon in the form of a child. Mishka reacted hysterically, calling Akyev the demon. Zhota recounted Mishka's tale to Akyev, telling him that he believed the child. Akyev was less inclined to believe Mishka's story than that of the Patriarchs (who had ordered him to hunt the "demon" down), and attacked Zhota, telling him that if he killed Mishka himself, his transgressions would be forgiven. In the fight, the head of Mishka's mother spilled out of Akyev's bag, confirming that Akyev was the "demon" that had killed Mishka's fellows. After a grueling fight, Zhota felled Akyev.
After awhile, Mishka played a tune again. Zhota told him that the "demon" who had killed his mother was no such thing, but he was dead nonetheless. He unbound Mishka and took him to his mother's head, giving him a chance to say goodbye. Mishka refused, simply stating "I don't need to. I have the song." With that, Zhota led Mishka to Ivgorod, determined to reveal the truth of what had happened.

======================================================================
PAGE: Nadya
CATEGORIES: Characters
URL: https://diablo.fandom.com/wiki/Nadya
======================================================================

Nadya
Gender
Female
Race
Human
Ethnicity
Askari
Affiliation
Askari
Class
Amazon
Appearances
Diablo Immortal
Nadya
is an
amazon
hailing from
Skartara
. At a time, she participated in the burden run of
Philios Games
. Though she'd trained for years for the event, her kindness caused her to lose the race.
Biography
After years of training, Nadya joined in the burden run to the base of
Karcheus
. Her island of
Skartara
had rarely won, but victors commanded glory,
gold
and station upon
the seas
.
Many of the repeat contestants from
Philios
wore resplendent
armor
with symbols of their villages, heavy laden to show their strength. Nadya's armor was lean and unornamented.
At the start of the race, Nadya kept pace with her competitors over the leaf-littered floor of the jungle. Suddenly, it began to rain heavily.
While the forest floor surged and soil cascaded beneath them, runners wearing the heaviest armor fell, and were trampled by those behind. By then, Nadya was taking the lead.
From her position, Nadya was a mere league from Karcheus. She saw cruel joy in the faces of the other lead runners as they sped away from the injured. They did not even look back as she slowed.
The others streamed past Nadya as she helped fallen runners from the mud. She reached Karcheus last, won no gold or titles, and was uncelebrated in her village. Nadya no longer cared, her pride was unwavering.
Legacy
The victorious racers of Philios carried their triumphs to sea as soldiers, and took up positions of influence above their peers. They spoke boldly of their competition, and argued fruitlessly about which of them had run the most perfect race.
Meanwhile, Skartara never acknowledged Nadya's participation, yet this did not shake her confidence. Victory in the eyes of others is longer-lasting than victory alone, but it is hardly eternal.
In-game
Nadya is mentioned in
Diablo Immortal
, in the flavor text of
Windloft Perfection
item set
.

======================================================================
PAGE: Nan
CATEGORIES: Characters
URL: https://diablo.fandom.com/wiki/Nan
======================================================================

"As I write this testimony, I understand that in all likelihood I ought to be hanged for it, and not for nothing. I am as guilty as sin in this matter. I won’t attempt to defend myself or persuade anyone I was innocent, because nobody would believe it, and because I wasn’t. How I loved her!-in what agonies I feared her, and fear for her!-how contemptible she was, that miserable creature who even now folk call the “Countess,” she who believes herself the Rose of Khanduras!"
- Nan
(
src
)
Nan
Gender
Female
Race
Human
Affiliation
Noble family of the
Big House
(formerly)
Occupation
Servant
Status
Deceased
Appearances
The Rose of Khanduras
Nan
was a servant of
the Countess
before her overthrow.
Biography
Ancestry
Nan’s mother was a distant cousin to the family who lived in the
Big House
, and served as a lady-in-waiting to the mother of
the Countess
. She fell in love with a blacksmith, and went to live in the swamps.
Early Life
"Now you may say that I am a coward. But no cowards grew up in the marshes, and it was a hard life, even before all that happened."
- Nan
(
src
)
Nan grew up in the marshes of northern
Khanduras
. It was a hard life. As a child, her granfer (her father’s father) told her that the noble family who ruled from the
Big House
practiced bride-theft and groom-theft. She could believe it, but found it easier to believe that the family married themselves and kin and cousins in order to keep their bloodline pure. Her granfer also discouraged her from preening, for in the swamp, becauty was both a snare and a foxlight.
Nan was taught how to read and write, due to her mother’s noble origins. Her granfer loved her, but despised her mother. Nan did most of the work in the house, maintaining it, and oiling her father’s tools, while her parents mooned over each other.
When Nan was around 15/16 years old, her mother died, and her father died the year after that, as according to Nan, he loved his wife far more than his daughter, and with his wife dead, there was nothing left to live for.
In Service to the Countess=
First Meetings
"How dare you not come when I want you? You ‘’’will’’’ come, I say.”
I say I won’t, so it’s your will against mine. I’m bigger than you by a head, stronger in my arms, and I could certainly throw you back through that door if I had a mind to it. What now, my lady?"
- The Countess and Nan meet for the first time
(
src
)
At the age of eighteen, Nan’s fortunes changed. The Countess, two years her junior, had seen her outside the Big House, and had taken a fancy to Nan’s looks. Her granfer informed her that she was wanted as a servant in the Big House, to which Nan refused. He pleaded, as did her neighbors, for no-one wanted the wrath of the noble family brought down on them. A man came down from the Big House every day for a sennight, cozening or begging or threatening, before at last, the Countess herself came down, mounted on a horse. She rode up to Nan’s house.
Nan was entranced with the Countess’s beauty and mannerisms, but still refused, at least at first. The Countess mixed compliments and insults alike, until finally, Nan relented, saying that she’d come, but leave at the end of spring if things didn’t suit her.
The First Two Years
{{Quote|Ah, for that was how she mastered me! I would bluster and act an old woman and nag and scold, for I think she rather enjoyed this maternal playacting: even liked me to prose about her behavior and call her beastly, as she turned that flowerlike face to me in wonderment. Nobody had ever cared to criticize her before, and she listened to my criticisms as thought I were some exotic bird she was keeping, trilling for her entertainment. I thought at one time I was educating her—but I know better now.
Nan ended up working for the family; something that was possible only due to her blood relation to them, however distant. Their working relationship was a mixture of insults and flirting, and over time, Nan fell into the roleplay, in addition to her duties as a servant. Under Nan’s guidance, the Countess became more elegant and less wild. The relationship between Nan and the Countess was not mirrored by the rest of the family; Nan loathed them, and Nan was told more than once by an uncle of the Countess that she would be dismissed if they could find someone else to ‘tame’ the Countess.’ After hearing of this, the Countess’s eyes went black, and soon after, the uncle fell off his horse, breaking his back. The Countess was so unmoved and uninterested in the incident that Nan hardly dared think she had any part in it.
Two years passed, over which the Countess became more refined, and better able to control her temper. Various men courted her, and the Countess strung them along, to both her and Nan’s amusement. However, she also turned down nobles, including those of “better blood.” Her behaviour enraged her family, but Nan stuck by her mistress. Nan personally considered nobody handsome enough for her, though prayed a king would come and take her away.
The Comtessa
"This will be an ugly part of my confession, but I must write it all. I still don’t know who the Comtessa is, was, or
what
she was, which is perhaps the better question. I cannot even write down her full name, for when she announced it to us, her and her whole riotous throng of followers and courtiers and parasites, it was much too long and grand to remember."
- Nan
(
src
)
One autumn night, a royal family arrived at the Big House. All of them youthful, all of them beautiful, all of them apparently unbothered by the cold. And foremost among them was
the Comtessa
. Nan was taken aback by the Comtessa’s beauty, but was suspicious; the retinue claimed they were traveling through Khanduras on pilgrimage, but Nan didn’t believe it. She Comtessa asked permission of the house to rest there, and Nan saw her eyes lingering on the Countess as she said it.
The Comtessa flattered the Countess, who, enraptured, demanded that rooms be made for the traveling party. Nan was assigned to this task and loathed it—the guests never showed their teeth, and they walked too softly for her liking. Furthermore, there was no smell about them, despite the distance they had travelled on horseback. However, the Countess was enraptured, and her tastes in clothing changed overnight. The old relationship between Nan and the Countess evaporated.
Things got worse for the house, as the Countess lavished the Comtessa with the wealth of their coffers, sending her family into fear and despair. The servants were similarly uneasy. Still, after a fortnight, the Comtessa declared that she and her retinue would depart, before the weather made it impossible to travel over the mountains. The Countess declared that they were already impassable, and the Comtessa declared that they would hold a party to cheer her up. Nan suspected that this was a routine of the Comtessa—arrive in a place, squat as long as she dared, and leave before too many questions were asked.
The party was riotous—so riotous that Nan went to the other servants’ quarters and told them to lock their doors and not answer for anyone, especially if they were young and good looking. An hour before dawn, the Countess finally returned to her quarters; her dress was torn, her hair in disarray, and she was ashen—so grey faced and childlike that Nan put her to bed immediately. When she undressed her gown, Nan noticed that it appeared like human hands had torn it open, and one edge was splattered with what Nan assumed was dry wine. The Countess whispered that the Comtessa had shown her “so many things,” but what these things were, she wouldn’t say.
In the morning, the retinue were gone, and the Countess had gone with them.
The keep went into an uproar, not even noticing that a few servants had gone missing as well. Nan suspected that the Comtessa had practiced bride-theft, though had no doubt that the Countess had gone willingly. Eventually, the Countess was brought home, apparently unhurt save for a shallow knife slit at the side of her throat. She could not say if anyone had attacked her. Nan put her to bed and refused to let the priests bleed her more. Nan considered the matter closed.
Sins of Spring
"That was the hideous winter. Now I write of the sins of the spring, and the hideous summer that burns upon us even now. I do not know how I will write, but I must. In the end someone will find out truly what she is, and my only hope for forgiveness is that I will assist that end, in some future I will never see."
- Nan
(
src
)
Winter came to Khanduras, and the Countess deteriorated. Nan nursed her, but it did no good, as the Countess became ever more ill, and the priests could not identify her condition. Eventually, she seemed to recover—sadder, but wiser, at least in Nan’s mind. However, their old playful dynamic was gone, as the Countess longed for the Comtessa, and nothing could bring her satisfaction. Nan became sick herself, and noticed that the Countess had become more cruel. She chastised her, but it was pitiful beratement, as Nan was terrified by the woman the Countess had turned into. Furthermore, the Countess was obsessed with her beauty, and Nan mixed herbal remedies of every kind, but nothing suited.
A new level of depravity revealed itself when Nan found the Countess in her bath tub as she so often was. A girl was stripped to the waist, and her naked arm was extended in her mistress’s grasp. The arm was slit from wrist to elbow, and the blood flowed over the Countess’s face, her neck, the very water of the bath. Nan bandaged the girl’s arm, led her away from the Countess and her mocking laughter, took the girl to her village, and told her mother that she did not suit, and would not be coming back. She returned to the Countess, who appeared like her old self, calling her “Sweet Nan.”
Part of Nan rejoiced to see the Countess as her old self, but the other part knew what was coming. One girl after another was bled in the same way, and each time, Nan led them out of the Big House, and returned to see the Countess rejuvenated. Nan knew, deep down, that the Countess would eventually kill, and so it happened, as a girl’s arms were slit to ribbons, and the blood drained into the tub, bereft of water. The Countess, bathing in blood, told Nan to “take out the rubbish.”
Nan did just that. She wrapped the dead girl in sacking, and put her in the cellar. Afterward, she lay at the Countess’s bed, pleading wit her to never do such a thing again. The Countess, barely listening, took up her title of “Rose of Khanduras.” For months, Nan had known that her mistress was mad, but this was something deeper than madness, more monstrous than lovesickness. Nan cursed the Comtessa for what she’d turned the Countess into.
Sins of Summer
"There you are, Nan. I have been waiting an age. You need to wash my hair. How ugly and frightened my maid appears this morning! I would stop being so ugly immediately, if I were you. Understand that you are now the last beautiful girl left alive, my beloved."
- The Countess
(
src
)
The Countess killed again before spring had turned into summer, and this time, with clear intent. One girl after another was murdered, their blood drained for the Countess to bathe in, and still, Nan played along. Boys were killed as well, and Nan saw that the Countess’s blood moved with her after being shed, and that her strength had increased beyond any normal
human
. Nan continued to serve, helping with the bleeding, and hiding the bodies in the cellar. Looking back on these events, as to why she did this, Nan stated that it was because the Countess was her mistress, and she obeyed. Perhaps if she continued to serve, the Countess would listen to her, and her violence would stop.
Whatever Nan’s rationalizations, the other servants knew that something was going on, and refused to wait on the Countess at all. Eventually, the priests rose up and told the family that the Countess ought to be sent to a convent or cloister, and an heir found from elsewhere. The Countess took this in good cheer, and Nan told her that they would run away together. Nan truly intended to leave with her, and believed that if they did so, they would spare the village of losing the last of its girls. If they took enough gowns and jewels, they might be able to make it to a city and remove themselves from the sight of peasants.
It never happened. The next morning, most of the priests were dead, and all of the family; necks broken, throats open, blood splashed everywhere. The servants and a few chaplains fled, screaming, many driven mad with terror. Soon, only Nan and the Countess were left in the tower. The Countess, examining her reflection in the mirror, greeted Nan, and advised herself to stop being ugly, for after all, she was the last beautiful girl left alive.
Nan fled. More than anything, that the Countess had finally called her “beloved” rocked her to her core.
Testimony
"But she was my mistress and deep in my bones remains my mistress still, to the end of her days and mine, whatever other name she has stolen for herself: and these guilty days of my own will surely end soon. I am not certain to live after what comes next. If I am to defend myself, I will say only that I was a girl, and that my mistress was not just as beautiful as everyone said, but more so. Upon opon a time, that monstrous Countess was the loveliest creature anyone ever laid eyes upon: but to me, she was just as willful and pig-ignorant and miserable a child who ever grew up in the fens."
- Nan
(
src
)
After escaping the Old House, Nan’s role in the Countess’s actions was hazy. Because the clergy were unable to talk any sense, they couldn’t implicate her. A number of crofters wanted to burn Nan at the stake, but her granfer spoke in her defense. Nan lied, and said she knew nothing of the murdered girls. Whether they believed it or not was irrelevant, as the villagers prepared to storm the keep at sunrise.
Nan wrote her testimony. She understood that it was likely she would be hanged, and considered herself guilty. However, even then, she could not abandon her love for the Countess.
Personality and Traits
Nan rarely used her birthname (“Nan” was a nickname used by the Countess).
Nan considered herself “very pretty for what [she] was,” with roses in her cheeks, and was not pallid like the other girls of the swamps. However, she was taught not to flaunt her appearance. She was “strong as a little horse.” She had black hair and blue eyes.
She disliked priests and clergy. By the end of her service to the Countess, she was consumed with self-loathing.

======================================================================
PAGE: Nerissa Natoli
CATEGORIES: Characters
URL: https://diablo.fandom.com/wiki/Nerissa_Natoli
======================================================================

Nerissa Natoli
Gender
Female
Race
Human
Affiliation
Westmarch
House Natoli
Occupation
Noblewoman
Relatives
Elizabeth
(sister)
Ashton Natoli
(husband)
Status
Deceased
Appearances
Turn of a Card
Nerissa Natoli
was a
Westmarch
noble, who lived in the country's
capital
. She excelled in playing cards and reading the faces of her opponents. While she never gambled as liberally as her husband, she emptied the purses of more than one rival in "friendly" card games, such as
Destiny
or
Wild Geese
(she particuarly excelled in this game).
Biography
Nerissa was married to
Ashton Natoli
; a good man, in her eyes, but one who had taking to drinking and gambling, draining the coffers of
House Natoli
in the process. At some point he vanished, taking what remained of the family fortune with him. Thus, over the period of a year, Nerissa was forced to deal with the creditors, as her standard of living was reduced as she struggled to pay off her husband's debts. She also had to provide for her sister,
Elizabeth
, and while
strange creatures
were reported in Westmarch. Things reached such a bad state that she knew she was at risk of losing her manor, per
Vincent Dastin
's unwillingness to collect Ashton's debts any longer.
On the same night as Dastin's refusal, she was picked up in a carriage by
Carlotta
, who claimed to be an old friend of the family. She was aware of Nerissa's situation, and offered her a way out. She asked if she played cards, to which Nerissa responded in the affirmative. Thus, Carlotta arranged to come to Nerissa's manor the following evening. Nerissa guessed that Carlotta was sitting on a fortune, and that she wanted to intentionally lose it through a card game so that she wouldn't be seen giving out her wealth as an act of charity.
The next evening came, and Carlotta arrived. As they discussed the stakes, Nerissa offered what was left of her jewelry. Carlotta wasn't interested, and asked Nerissa what she valued most in the world. Nerissa, assuming that this was a game of social niceity, responded that what she desired most was to see her husband returned, sober, and with his wealth restored. In return, she wagered anything of hers that Carlotta desired. Carlotta agreed, and explained the rules of the game. They would each pick three cards, drawing them one at a time. By the end, whoever held the highest card would win. Nerissa was put off, knowing that this would be a competition of luck rather than skill, but agreed to take part. The game was played, and Nerissa won. Carlotta saw herself out, saying that she would come tomorrow night, if Nerissa chose, but warned her to choose carefully. And with that she left. The same night, a commoner arrived at her manor, bringing Ashton's body to be buried. He had nothing on him, and Nerissa had to foot the bill for the delivery fee.
Nerissa was aghast. She suspected Carlotta of
witchcraft
, but rationalized that it had to be a coincidence. She decided to have Carlotta return, in hope of getting the fortune she had offered. Carlotta arrived, and Nerissa offered the same stakes—anything that Carlotta desired, against a dowry for Elizabeth. She was put off by how Carlotta seemed different, more "hungry," but the game was played, and again, Nerissa won. Carlotta exited the manor before she could discuss payment of the dowry. She again warned Nerissa to consider the stakes, and that if she wished her to return (again), she would do so on the morrow. Nonetheless, Carlotta apparently honored her word, as a boy arrived with an envelope, containing a dowry. Apparently, Viscount
Delfinus
was a distant relation of House Natoli, and he'd just passed away. Before he died, the letter claimed, he had set aside funds for his youngest unmarried relations. She shared the news with Elizabeth, who was overjoyed. All seemed well...
...at least it did until Elizabeth collided with
Maurice
, their servant, who was holding an oil lamp. Elizabeth caught on fire as the flames spread, and while healers were able to save her life, her face was severely disfigured. It was now obvious to Nerissa that Carlotta was behind this. Twice she'd got what she wanted, and twice what she'd wanted had been ripped away. Thus, she resolved for a final game, one that she would win, no matter what. So the next night, Carlotta arrived, her visage still offputting, even as Nerissa refused to give her the usual social nicities. Regardless, Nerissa dictated the stakes. She would have Elizabeth's happiness and beauty restored, and it would be done so for the duration of the game, until she turned her last card. Carlotta resisted, but eventually acquiesed, and sure enough, Elizabeth's beauty was restored, though she was in a daze. Nerissa bid her goodbye as the game began. As it neared its end, with Nerissa waiting to turn her card, as Carlotta urged her to bring it to an end, Nerissa did so, by plunging a siletto into her own chest. Carlotta tried to save her, but it was too late. Nerissa was dead. And what was more, Carlotta had lost, for Nerissa had dictated that the terms of the bargain be "until I draw my last card." Now, it was an action that she could never undertake. Losing her old vigor, Carlotta left the manor, commenting "well played, my dear. Well played indeed."

======================================================================
PAGE: Norrec Vizharan
CATEGORIES: Characters
URL: https://diablo.fandom.com/wiki/Norrec_Vizharan
======================================================================

Norrec Vizharan
Title
Warlord of Blood (satirically)
The Fool
Gender
Male
Race
Human
Relatives
Bartuc
(ancestor, †)
Kara Nightshadow
(partner)
Status
Unknown
Appearances
Legacy of Blood
Norrec Vizharan
is the protagonist of
Richard A. Knaak
's
Diablo
novel
Legacy of Blood
.
He owns the armour of Bartuc, Warlord of Blood. In his time, he often travelled with his friends,
Sadun
and
Fauztin
, looking for treasure for their own spending purposes. Norrec, who grew up in Westmarch, worked as a mercenary for most of his life.
Norrec adventured with a party of two mercenaries into a labyrinth. The curse of the armour began when he equipped a gauntlet belonging to Bartuc, the Warlord of Blood. The gauntlet was unable to be removed from his hand and took control of him, causing the deaths of Sadun and Fauztin. After falling unconscious shortly after, he awoke with the rest of the armour stuck on.
The armor gave its wearer great strength and the ability to summon and command demons, though Norrec had almost no control of this ability as long as he had worn it. Norrec tried once to commit suicide but this went against the armour's plan, and it began to take control of his body to keep him alive, needing him as a host. Its goal was to reunite with its missing piece, the helmet, and resurrect the spirit of Bartuc.
Trivia
Norrec's last name means "servant of the Vizjerei" in the old tongue.

PAGE: Nuhat
CATEGORIES: Characters
URL: https://diablo.fandom.com/wiki/Nuhat
======================================================================

"The living use their words frivolously, with little knowledge of how many they have to spare. Yet when the dead speak, each word is to be treasured. This is proof of transcendence."
- Nuhat
(
src
)
Nuhat
Title
The Flagellant
Gender
Male
Race
Human
Ethnicity
Kehjistan
Affiliation
Skatsim
Status
Deceased
Appearances
Diablo Immortal
(mentioned only)
Nuhat
was a practitioner of
Skatsim
around the period of the
Zakarum Inquisition
. He protested against the violence the Inquisitors brought to his hometown, and was executed for it.
Biography
In the center of town, Nuhat pierced his palm full through with the cross of the
Zakarum
to protest the Inquisition, and the violence they brought to
Kehjistan
.
When the Zakarumites who captured relics of Skatsim and murdered their keepers became cursed—their eyes turned rheumy and black-irised, the
High Inquisitor
was certain Nuhat held the secret, and questioned him fervently.
After months
of torture, Nuhat agreed to lift the curse. He touched his severed thumb to the foreheads of his captors. The inquisitors expected
fire
to rain down, but instead darkness lifted from their eyes, and their sight returned.
The High Inquisitor was furious that the curse they had failed to lift was banished by Nuhat in mere moments. For that, he demanded Nuhat renounce Skatsim.
Nuhat refused to deny his faith, and the High Inquisitor condemned the Flagellant to an excruciating
death
, which the inquisitors executed without delay.
Even with the
life
bled from Nuhat's throat, his dead mouth croaked that
humanity
was a lie, that people were simply
beasts
in hiding. The inquisitors tarred his
corpse
, but repeated his words.
In-game
Nuhat is mentioned in
Diablo Immortal
, in the flavor text of
Grace of the Flagellant
item set
.
Trivia
This section contains facts and trivia relevant to this article.
The pieces of the item set implies that Nuhat had the soles of his feet torn,
hand rent,
an eye ruined,
and a thumb severed.
Nuhat was killed by having his throat slit,
and after that, his
corpse
was disemboweled,
and its tongue mangled.

======================================================================
PAGE: Oswen
CATEGORIES: Characters
URL: https://diablo.fandom.com/wiki/Oswen
======================================================================

Oswen
Gender
Male
Race
Human
Affiliation
Nevesk
Lilith
Status
Deceased
Appearances
Diablo IV
Oswen
was a resident of
Nevesk
.
Biography
Oswen and Vani meet the Wanderer
In
1336
, while attending a service at the Nevesk chapel,
Lilith
appeared before Oswen and his fellow villagers, seducing him and the other villagers into following her. While the
Cathedral of Light
priest urged them to resist Lilith, his words fell on deaf ears, and Oswen and the rest of the villagers beat him to
death
. They then placed the headless body in
Icehowl Ruins
, where
Iosef
later found it. Upon his arrival into Nevesk, Oswen and the townsfolk drugged Iosef, with Oswen and
Vani
locking him in a shed. Iosef rambled like a madman about
demons
and bit Oswen's hand. Afterwards,
the Wanderer
entered the shed to investigate. Vani lied to the Wander, saying Iosef came to the village as a madman, yelling about what he had seen inside the ruins. While the Wanderer spoke with Vani, Oswen remained outside by the shed.
Oswen prepares the Wanderer for sacrifice
After clearing out the ruins, the Wanderer returned to Nevesk, where Oswen told them that Iosef punched him in the gut and escaped into the nearby woods. The townsfolk then threw a celebration in order to drug the Wanderer. After passing out, Oswen hauled the unconscious Wanderer into a barn using the back of a wagon. Along the way he hummed a melody. Upon entering the barn, Oswen forced the Wanderer to ingest
blood petals
. After this, he prepareed for a sacrificial ritual. While Oswen sharpened his knife, Iosef snuck into the barn and struck him in the back of the head with an iron rod, killing him.
In-game
Oswen is an
NPC
in
Diablo IV
. He is found in
Nevesk
in the game's
prologue
. He is first introduced inside a shack with
Vani
and
Iosef
as part of the "
Dusk on the Mountain
"
quest
.
Quotes
During
Dusk on the Mountain
, before entering

Perithan

Biography
Perithan resided in Margrave alongside his brother,
Lacthan
. Unlike Lacthan, he was a troublemaker, and generally detested by the other villagers.
In
1336
, Perithan made a deal with a group of bandits. He would lead a group of merchants through a mountain pass, where the bandits would attack. They assured him that it would be a clean job, that the merchants would be robbed, but left unharmed. However, when the attack came, the bandits began killing the merchants. Not wanting to kill anyone himself, Perithan ran, but was caught, and brought back to the bandits'
hideout
, where he was punished.
Later, Lacthan arrived at the hideout alongside
the Wanderer
, where they found Perithan. Perithan explained what had happened, and while Lacthan believed him, he pointed out that no-one else in Margrave would. He said they would head through the hideout's smuggler tunnels, head south, and start over. The Wanderer agreed to remain silent as to what had happened.

in

"

PAGE: Quentin Sharpe
CATEGORIES: Characters
URL: https://diablo.fandom.com/wiki/Quentin_Sharpe
======================================================================

Quentin Sharpe
Gender
Male
Race
Human
Affiliation
Westmarch
Occupation
Explorer
Status
Deceased
Appearances
Diablo III: Reaper of Souls
"I did not believe the legends—all true! This island, it rots you from within. We never should have come here..."
- Quentin Sharpe's last words
(
src
)
Quentin Sharpe
is a minor character in the
Greyhollow Island
storyline in
Act V
of
Diablo III
.
Biography
Sharpe and his team came to Greyhollow island against their will after a wave hit their ship and smashed it at the rocks of the island's shores. They were therefore forced to stay there and wait for rescue, for at least a month. The explorer then decided to research the land, which he believed was a myth.
The entire crew of Sharpe's team died over time, from illness, madness, or for no apparent reason, unable to withstand the evil of
Nereza
poisoning them. Sharpe lived longest of them, hiding in the caves.
Sharpe's last moments
After meeting
Rayeld
, Sharpe tried to kill him (when the Crazed Man attacked one of his crewmen). Quentin later tried countless times to kill The Crazed Man, but to no avail, as the cursed priest could not die permanently. After one such attempt, wounded gravely, Sharpe tried to reach the
Waypoint
in desperation. He witnessed
the Nephalem
coming through it, but died from blood loss before he could have been helped.
In-game
Quentin Sharpe dies immediately as the Nephalem teleports to the island. His journal,
Explorer's Log
, can be found across the island, including all caves. One of them,
Sharpe's Cove
, bears his name.
Trivia
This section contains facts and trivia relevant to this article.
He shares voice, model and portrait with the
Wounded Man
in
Leoric's Manor
.

======================================================================
PAGE: Rayeld
CATEGORIES: Characters
URL: https://diablo.fandom.com/wiki/Rayeld
======================================================================

Rayeld the Younger
Title
The Crazed Man
Gender
Male
Race
Human
Affiliation
Greyhollow Island
Occupation
Priest of
Nereza
Relatives
High Cleric
(father)
Status
Alive
Appearances
Diablo III: Reaper of Souls
Rayeld the Younger
, also known as
The Crazed Man
, is a priest of
Nereza
inhabiting the
Greyhollow Island
.
Biography
Son of the
High Cleric
, Rayeld was preparing since childhood to become the High Cleric himself. Taught by his father that human sacrifices to Nereza are necessary to keep the island free of evil, he awaited the time when he himself would bring offerings. However, when the time came, he could not bring himself to do so. After he performed ritual murders himself, Rayeld became disgusted with what the cult was doing. Doubting his faith, he decided to put an end to sacrifices.
At one point, unable to bring himself to kill a girl named
Sara
in the name of Nereza, Rayeld murdered his father, fled with the girl (other cultists, shocked by the incident, did not even try to interfere), rushed to the top of the
Ancient Tower
, and plunged his sacrificial dagger into Nereza's chest. Before she died, he saw the inhuman gaze of her eyes, and realized that Nereza was no goddess, but a
demon
, and the evil the sacrifices were to prevent was not from the outside world, but from herself.
The dying demon killed Sara with her last breath, and her essence went through Rayeld into the island itself, cursing the land and the priest, condemning him to eternal torment for his sacrilege. Rayeld was welcomed as a hero by his people when they found out what he did, yet he realized that the corruption from Nereza's evil would eventually ravage the island. It indeed happened, the land becoming uninhabitable: any human stepping on its shores would be driven insane, if not killed earlier by the unseen evil force.
Rayeld as The Crazed Man
Rayeld attempted to contain the evil, not allowing it to expand to other lands. To do so, he erected magical wards and kept Nereza's spirit pacified by rituals and sacrifices (ironically, doing exactly what he was raised for, with the same purpose he once believed to be his path). Losing his sanity, he became known as The Crazed Man, living as a hermit on the island, only rarely to be seen by travelers and sailors coming to the shore (mostly from shipwrecks).
Using his knowledge of the binding rituals, Rayeld
magically
enslaved majority of the creatures on the island, either by prayers, sacrifices, or simply by carving the warding runes into their skin. Though he himself eventually forgot how and why did he do this, he deeply regretted that he was forced to bind living beings to his will.
Sasquatches
,
Bone Breakers
,
Wildwood Bulwarks
,
Shipwrecked Souls
,
Wood Specters
and (probably) more creatures of the island were all controlled by him. Rayeld even remarks in his records that he cannot remember if Sasquatches were humans turned feral by evil of the island, or he himself turned them into beasts to protect them from Nereza's corruption.
Abyssals
,
Amputators
and
Flesh Harvesters
, who Rayeld could not control, he battled until forcing them to remain in their
caves
, though he soon learned that as long as the sea people's idols are not disturbed, they would not be aggressive in the first place.
Nereza's curse effectively made Rayeld immortal (of which he was perfectly aware), bringing him back from the dead should he be killed, to ensure his eternal torture. The only way to ensure his release would be to cleanse his spirit at the site of Nereza's death.
In-game
The Crazed Man
is a
Super Unique
foe found on the Greyhollow Island in
Act V
of
Diablo III
, in
Adventure Mode
only. He can be found at one of two possible locations: either amidst the bone totems, or in front of the sacrificial altar.
In either case, he will not be hostile to the player, and in fact, will not even acknowledge their presence, being busy tending to the binding rituals. If talked to, or if his ritual is interfered with, he will turn hostile.
Altar
: if spoken to, The Crazed Man will attack, starting the event
Binding Evil
.
Totems
: if the Pillar of Cupidity is touched, The Crazed Man will attack, starting the event
Ghost Prison
.
In either case, he will attack by hurling darkfire bolts that deal tremendous damage from afar. He has no other abilities. However, other monsters in the area will protect him, depending on the event.
He can also be encountered during the unmarked event atop the
Forsaken Repose
, if player touches any of his satchels (of
Testament of My Failure
tome
) after they collect both tomes. This opens a purple portal to the top of
Ancient Tower
, at the very site where Rayeld killed Nereza. He can then be talked to, and will tell that he waited for a long time for
the Nephalem
to come to this place since their last visit.
He will then ask the Nephalem to cleanse his spirit. The player must first destroy his mortal form at the tower. This will be complicated due to Crazed Man gaining an extra ability to summon a slowly moving broad wall of darkfire, which, if touched by player, will deal significant damage over time. Moreover, he will now hurl darkfire bolts in clusters of three, being hit by all three is enough to kill an adequately geared hero outright.
If defeated, his ghost is released, continuing to fight on its own. In spirit form, he gains Illusionist affix, his darkfire bolts are replaced with equally powerful spirit bolts, and instead of the wave of flame, he will launch homing black gouts of spirit fire, which expire after short time.
Killing him in his spirit form will lift the curse, supposedly liberating his soul, and opening the portal back to the island.
Crazed Man tending to his totems
Crazed Man at his altar
Portal to Forsaken Repose
Crazed Man met atop the tower
Crazed Man's soul cleansed
Quotes
Benedictus es deam Nereza maximum est. Nostra digni gratia tua et amor.
(roughly translated from Latin as
You are the most blessed of all, goddess Nereza. May we be worthy of your love.
)
The island must be fed lest the evil spread.
You must submit or everyone will die! Why do you fight me?
What have you... wait. We've done this before, haven't we?
What have you done? The totems must remain intact. The island demands it!
(when touching the Pillar of Cupidity)
I know you. You killed me before, didn't you? Or hasn't that happened yet?
We're going to fight again? Will you kill me this time, or will I kill you? No matter what happens, the island feeds!
What? How dare you! I have spent lifetimes, and you, you... aaagh!
Why do you stop me? Can't you hear the island? She's crying. She must be fed!
You are finally here. It has been long years since I saw you last. There is only one thing left, now. My spirit must be cleansed.
(when met atop the tower)
Thank you, thank you. I have waited for this respite for so long. You have freed me from my torment.
(when freed from the curse)
These... things have no body, they are simple constructs of magical energy, amplified and contained by their armor. As for who created them, I cannot say. Hm... could I have done this?
(unused Bestiary entry)
Trivia
This section contains facts and trivia relevant to this article.
After the first time players kill him, The Crazed Man will react differently in every game to follow: he will state that the Nephalem has already killed him before. He is therefore the only monster in game to change his behavior after first death.
Putting his soul to rest atop the Ancient Tower will not prevent him from appearing in subsequent games. Moreover, he can even be encountered (and killed) in the very same game where his curse has been lifted after it happens, if one does not talk to him on the island prior to entering the portal.

Biography
"Ah yes, the unreasonable one I spoke of earlier. I loved her every inch of my heart before it went black as coal."
"Where is she now?"

- Lyndon and

======================================================================
PAGE: Rebirth
CATEGORIES: Characters
URL: https://diablo.fandom.com/wiki/Rebirth
======================================================================

Rebirth
is the process by which a non-Seasonal character can be turned into a
Seasonal
one in
Diablo III
. They are reset to level 1 with no gear or other progression, just like any other new Seasonal character. This allows a a pre-existing character to join the Season, and allows a player who already has the maximum number of characters to participate without deleting and recreating any characters.
This option has been available since Season 5.
Usage
Rebirth confirmation screen
The Rebirth option is shown on the character selection section of the main menu before starting a game. It can only be used on three characters per season. A confirmation box explains the process before completing the rebirth. The player may select "normal" Seasonal mode or
Solo Self Found
mode. Upon accepting, the character will be marked as Seasonal, and all forms of character progress will be reset:
The hero is set to
Level
1 with 0
experience
, with the associated lack of
skills
and stats
All items equipped or in inventory are mailed to the non-Seasonal side of the account. The player has 30 days to retrieve them before they are lost.
Campaign progress is reset
Armory
profiles are erased
Only their choice of name, class, gender, and
Hardcore
status is preserved. In almost every way it is as if the original character had been deleted, and a new Seasonal one was created with the same character creation choices, with the exception of mailing the previous items.
Note that many forms of progression are actually stored "per account" rather than "per character" - or more accurately, per
game mode
on the account. These aspects, such as
Paragon
levels,
artisan
advancement, and the shared
stash
, are retained by the other non-Seasonal characters. If a player already has other Seasonal characters, the Rebirthed character would even gain the benefits of
their
account/mode-level progression, if any.
