Appearances
Diablo Immortal
The Curator
is an ageless simulacrum
created by
Zoltun Kulle
, and the guardian of his
library
.
Biography
Origins
"I can neither leave nor enter the secret archives. It is infuriating."
- The Curator on his predicament
(
src
)
A simulacrum of
Zoltun Kulle
, the Curator was created at some point prior to the
Wizard
's death,
in what was apparently a moment of Kulle's egomania getting the better of him.
It was meant to be the receptacle of Kulle's consciousness in the event of his
death
.
The Curator was created through living sand, like a number of Kulle's other creations (e.g.
golems
),
and possesses its creator's wit and focus, but without the egomania he manifested in his later years.
The duplicate was assigned to act as the curator of
Zoltun Kulle's Library
,
and ensure its continuance,
by minimizing
magical
decay.
Like Kulle's other constructs, it was kept on a tight leash. However, according to the Curator, "that [being constrained] has never stopped me before."
Over time, the library fell into disrepair.
Its central core shut down,
and as such, a pair of wards went up that prevented access to certain sections of the library,
including Kulle's secret archives.
Despite the Curator's efforts, he was unable to breach them,
much to his frustration. Additionally, he was unable to leave the library itself.
New Arrivals
"The library has been ravaged by time, and has fallen into disrepair. But it could be restored If you truly are no thief, then perhaps you will prove your innocence."
"What do you have in mind?"
First, I must regain my strength. And a myriad of monsters stand between us and the statue where that can happen. Considering my weakened state is your fault...I'll let you clear the way."
- The hero and the Curator meet
(
src
)
The Curator is first encountered
In the year
1270
, the duplicate barred entrance to the library to
the Shard-seeker
.
He believed the intruder(s) to be thieves, and despite their protests to the contrary, unleashed
Phantoms
upon them. After the Phantoms were destroyed, he engaged the intruder(s) directly.
He was defeated, and they explained that they weren't thieves, but rather, sought a way to destroy the Worldstone shards. The Curator stated that if Kulle knew of a way, he would have stored the information in his private archives. However, given his weakened state, he couldn't reach that location. He had to regain his strength, and ordered the hero(es) to clear the library of the creatures that infested it. Arriving at a statue that could restore his power, they found that its runes had been removed. He ordered the hero(es) to find them. With the runes restored, he led them to the library's central core, for to restore the library, they needed to bring the core back to life.
However, he couldn't reactivate the core, and ordered the hero(es) to obtain Kulle's journal, as it detailed the inner workings of the library.
Upon their return, the Curator studied the journal and concluded that the core was comprised of rock animated by living sand. As such,
magic
could not reactivate it. Unlike his master, bringing  the spark of
life
to artificial creations was beyond his abilities. He ordered them to head to the
Chaos Engine
, which they could use to extract the
essence
of life from a golem, and use it to power the core.
The Curator in the archives
The hero(es) returned with life essence, and the Curator used it to reactivate the core. With it, the wards that had thwarted the Curator for so long went down, much to his joy. He told the hero(es) to join him in the
Archive of Secrets
, where they would hopefully be able to discover how to destroy the Worldstone shards they carried. He presented to them a
tome
that recalled Kulle's experience in the
Dark Exile
, when he and
Tal Rasha
had defeated
Baal
. The tome contained Kulle's memories perfectly recorded, able to be experienced directly by any who read the work. They headed into
the Forbidden Archive
to read it. Along the way, the Curator questioned the wisdom of destroying the shards rather than utilizing them, but didn't press further. However, he hoped that the hero(es) would share their story with him.
The hero(es) entered Kulle's memories in the tome, where they learnt that only the weapon of an
archangel
could damage the Worldstone.
The Curator explained that Kulle only knew of two such weapons—
El'druin
, which was beyond their reach, and
Yl'nira
, currently located in the
Temple of Namari
on
Bilefen
.
With the library now under his control, he modified a
terminus
to take the hero(es) to the island, near the temple. He gave them permission to come and go through the library as they pleased, and told them to "try not to die before our next meeting." But if they did choose to leave, to do so quickly—he hated long goodbyes.
Afterwards, the Curator managed to regain control of a number of the library's Golems, but many remained wild and uncontrolled.
The Fractured Plane
"You've returned...and with a curio that does not belong to this world."
"It's a stone that your master once used to open the Fractured Plane."
"Ah yes, the Sumina Glass. it is a fount of unbound chaos and cyclical death. Even the master was wary of it. Count yourself fortunate that the magics it housed have faded."
- The Curator and the Shard-seeker
(
src
)
The Shard-seeker returned to the library with the
Sumina Glass
. Like Kulle before them, they sought to enter the
Fractured Plane
.
In-game
The Curator in-game
The Curator is encountered as an enemy at the start of the Library of Zoltun Kulle
questline
in
Diablo Immortal
. It starts by summoning
Mysterious Phantoms
in the quest "
Unseen Guardian
." Here, it goes under the moniker of "Mysterious Voice," using the same portrait as the
Mirrored World
monsters
. He is later fought directly.
In this fight, he is immune to
knockback
, and can
teleport
. He has the following attacks:
Sand Tornado: Sends a tornado out in a straight line.
Sand Lines: Sends lines of sand outwards from his base, damaging the player if they're touched.
Sand Projectiles: Sends out 'sand daggers' in a circular motion
Summon
Skeletal Guardian
After the boss fight, the Curator becomes an
NPC
, and will appear throughout the library at various points in its questline.
A
Rift Guardian
counterpart for the Curator exists via the
Sand Shaper
.
Personality and Traits
"You have proven trustworthy enough to come and go at your discretion, but should you choose to leave, do it quickly. I abhor long goodbyes. Try not to die before our next meeting, hm?"
- The Curator
(
src
)
The Curator
The Curator, in many ways, is similar to his creator—suspicious,
snide,
possessed of a dry wit, and possessing the need for both control
and knowledge.
Unlike his creator, he came to trust his companion(s), and even seemed to develop genuine affection for them.
Also like Kulle, the Curator possesses powers of his own, such as sand-based
magic
abilities,
and the ability to
teleport
.
He is also capable of operating Kulle's technological devices.
Trivia
This section contains facts and trivia relevant to this article.
The Curator as he appears on the loading screen
Based on early information, the Curator was apparently simply called "Zoltun Kulle," though was still explicitly a duplicate of the original character. It was stated to believe that it was the real Zoltun Kulle.
In the final version however, the character is called "the Curator," and is aware that Kulle is its creator.
When first encountered in the game's beta, the Curator states "he warned me you would come...and after a millennia, here you are." The timeframe of "millennia" however contradicted the
timeline
, where centuries passed between Kulle's death and the events of
Immortal
, not millennia. In the final version, this was changed to "centuries," fitting the timeline.

PAGE: The Mountebank
CATEGORIES: Characters
URL: https://diablo.fandom.com/wiki/The_Mountebank
======================================================================

"Why defy our "betters," contest their hypocrisies, and traduce their authority when it may cost us our lives? However indulgent it may be, a false existence is a shadow of a life lived according to one's wants."
- The Mountebank
(
src
)
The Mountebank
Gender
Female
Race
Human
Affiliation
Zakarum
(faux)
Occupation
Thief
Status
Deceased
Appearances
Diablo Immortal
(mentioned only)
The Mountebank
was a thief/agitant who drove the
Zakarum
from
Miettevin
.
Biography
The Mountebank gathered hundreds of written indulgences from the cloister of Miettevin by posing as a priest. She scattered them in the street, spurring anger against the faith's profiteers.
Later she infiltrated the church's reliquary to steal the jawbone of
Saint Alavaine
. She did this by having herself delivered to the church's cellar in a wine barrel. She poured the barrel into the reliquary as she ran, and left red bootprints in the nave.
This earned her the enmity of the local church, and the temple knights chased her to
Fogswell
, where they flanked her on both banks of the river. She dove into the water as they loosed their arrows, and a stray broadhead cored Prior
Niv
through the hand.
She gained a nemesis in the form of the
Paladin
Gurdannel
. He challenged her to a duel, and she accepted for it to be held at the
Frozen Foot of the Uxbers
. She delayed her arrival twice, and snow stranded Gurdannel's entourage, ruining his reputation.
The Mountebank later set the church's cloister on fire, using only a pitch and cotton-wrapped pipe. As she watched from the hills, Gurdannel caught her and ran her through, though she leapt to her
death
with a smile.
She fell to earth near the town square. Stolen indulgences fluttered about her like feathers. Once townsfolk recognized her
body
, they killed Gurdannel.
Legacy
The Mountebank's death sparked a violent upheaval and revolution
that led to the exile of the faith from Miettevin.
A statue was built in her honor in the square where she died.
In-game
The Mountebank is referenced in the item-text of
Untouchable Mountebank
item set
in
Diablo Immortal
.
References

======================================================================
PAGE: The Shepherd
CATEGORIES: Characters
URL: https://diablo.fandom.com/wiki/The_Shepherd
======================================================================

The Shepherd
Title
The Shepherd
Race
Human
Ethnicity
Caldeum
(presumed)
Occupation
Revolutionary
Status
Deceased
Appearances
Diablo Immortal
The Shepherd
is a mysterious figure that led a revolution against the corrupt
mages
of the
Yshari Sanctum
, around the time of the
Apprentices' Uprising
.
Biography
In
Caldeum
's slums, far from the splendored walls of the Yshari Sanctum, youths too fierce for the orphanages could claim a free meal in the Shepherd's almshouse.
To first-time visitors, the Shepherd asked how to deal with minds polluted by the use of
magic
. If their answers moved the Shepherd, they would receive a room, clothing, and a brace of knives.
The Shepherd trained their orphans in martial and mental discipline, and spoke at length of the calamitous power offered to mages within the Yshari Sanctum.
As the flock grew, the Shepherd had them eavesdrop on travelers and impersonate local criers. They shared stories of dangers within the Sanctum, stoking resentment.
The Shepherd's flock slew nine magi who abducted sacrifices in the slums, and collapsed one of the Sanctum's antechambers to prevent a contagion of lunacy from spreading.
Following the Apprentices' Uprising, a group of Sanctum magi captured the almshouse and the Shepherd. The flock fled to the
Borderlands
, but continued to hear the voice of the Shepherd, insisting on revenge.
The broken flock could not sleep for the incessance of the Shepherd's voice in their minds. After bitter arguments, they gathered three of their number who remained. Outnumbered and fearful, they set fire to the old almshouse in the dead of night, and the Shepherd grew quiet.
Legacy
The flock pawed through the soot and ashes of the burnt almshouse, but found only a single
body
. The magi had anticipated their coming, muzzled their prisoner, and departed. Bereft, the three disciples quit Caldeum for good, scattering throughout
Estuar
's alleys and alehouses.
In-game
The Shepherd is mentioned in
Diablo Immortal
, in the flavor text of the pieces of the
Shepherd's Call to Wolves
item set.

still lumbering across

, and killed many prisoners being held there.
Biography
"Thank you, champion. My servants are now free, but the curse over this place remains. Seek the Warden at the dungeon's center, and end his evil forever."
-
Queen Asylla
(
src
)
The Warden was Leoric's executioner during the
Darkening of Tristram
. He imprisoned and executed numerous innocents in the dungeons below
Leoric's Manor
.
He,
Leoric
, and
Lazarus
, discussed the fate of
Queen Asylla
.
Like numerous other prisoners under his watch, she too was executed. So horrific were the actions that the spirits of Asylla and the other innocents were tethered to the dungeons, unable to move on.
Two decades later
, the Warden was still present in the
hold
beneath
Leoric's Manor
, as an
undead
ghoul. He was stirred to action by
The Nephalem
, who had released the spirits of his victims. The Warden didn't take kindly to this, but was killed by The Nephalem.
The Chosen
speculated that the Warden's spirit had remained here because he had never been able to fully accept what he had done to the prisoners.
In-game
The Warden appears in "
The Imprisoned Angel
" in
Act I
of
Diablo III
. After completing the task of
Queen Asylla
, the Warden will appear in the center of the prison with his
ghoul
minions. After killing the Warden, one can gain passage to the torture areas of the castle.
He counts as an undead
Super Unique
enemy, and has Jailer, Desecrator and Molten monster affixes, as well as triple fireball ranged attack.
In
Adventure Mode
, one can access the Cursed Hold from both sides (
Halls of Agony
level 2 and
Highlands Passage
, or Halls of Agony level 3) in order to kill him faster should the Warden be nominated a target for the
bounty
.

This section contains facts and trivia relevant to this article.

Chain of Possession
,"
Parin
states that the axe was inhabited by the spirit of a demon. It is possible that the Woodsman is the demon itself, or alternatively, a
human
who became twisted into a demon/demonic form. That the axe is inhabited by a demon is later reiterated by Parin in "Legacy Unmade," though the events leave it open as to whether the Woodsman is the demon itself, or one of the
souls
the axe ensnared.

PAGE: Tremain the Priest
CATEGORIES: Characters
URL: https://diablo.fandom.com/wiki/Tremain_the_Priest

This page contains obsolete content
This article contains information that is no longer relevant to gameplay.
"All I can do now is pray for us all."
- Tremain
(
src
)
Tremain
Tremain the Priest
existed in pre-release versions of
Diablo
, and is not present in the final version of the game. He originally triggered the quest "
Archbishop Lazarus
".
Tremain also had his own quest, "Fleshdoom, Wielder of Shadowfang", where the player was tasked into killing said demon and retrieving the sword Shadowfang, to be destroyed by the priest's holy powers. However, when the player returned the demonblade to Tremain, he was to be consumed by hellfire and slain, with his soul presumably being trapped within the ebon blade. The quest was also was also cut from the game.
Personality and Traits
"His holiness is a wondrous man of great knowledge and understanding. He has shown me many cures for rare and deadly diseases. He brings me books and reagents for my work whenever he can. But I fear that he may some day take on some task that is too great even for him."
-
Pepin
(
src
)
Tremain was a kind and just man, known for his many talents. As holy man from an Ancient Order (presumably a
Zakarum
), he was a wielder of light, capable of both healing the wounded and also performing powerful exorcisms, as he seen by his ability to purge evil from the man who was possessed by the demon Fleshdoom. Tremain was admired and revered by the townsfolk of Tristram, particularly Pepin, who learned a lot from the priest.
While not a fighter himself, Tremain was supposedly powerful enough to hold himself against demons, as noted by him mentioning he was able to fight Fleshdoom before the demon fled into The Labyrinth beneath the
cathedral
. Tremain was also able to wander in and out of Tristram without being targeted by the cloaked riders, who were the demonic entities that would attack any villager who tried to leave the town.
Deckard Cain
noted that Tremain's ability to travel with little problems aided the Tristram in keeping some contact with the rest of the
kingdom
.
Despite his holy powers of exorcism, even Tremain was unable to purge the evil from the demonblade Shadowfang, which ultimately led to his demise.
Quest Text
"Archbishop Lazarus"
I seek a champion to undertake a serious duty, and the people of this town speak well of your courage and skill. The Arch-Bishop Lazarus, once King Leoric's most trusted advisor and a member of our order, has taken the path of evil. Not long ago Lazarus led a party of simple townsfolk into the labyrinth to find the King's missing son, Albrecht. Only a few of them escaped with their lives. Curse me for a fool! I should have suspected his veiled treachery then, for I have learned that it was Lazarus himself who kidnapped King Leoric's son and has since hidden him within the labyrinth. I still don't understand why the Arch-Bishop has turned to the darkness or what his interest is in Albrecht. Unless he means to sacrifice him at the full moon. That must be what he has planned! The survivors of his rescue party say that Lazarus was last seen running into the deepest bowels of the labyrinth, some sixteen levels beneath the cathedral. You must hurry and save the prince from the sacrificial blade of this demented fiend!
Why do you delay? Time is of the essence! The prince and the people of this kingdom are counting on you.
So, Lazarus has paid the price for his betrayal and justice is served. For your services this day, I bestow this mace unto you. Its name is Lightforge, and it is the holiest of our order's artifacts. As I am the last of this order, I entrust it to you. May the light guide you.
This is terrible! Lazarus will surely burn in hell for his horrific deed! Although the boy that you describe may not be our prince, I believe that Albrecht may yet be in danger. What ever vile power lay beneath the ground has assuredly gained a foothold in our world. All I can do now is pray for us all."
"Fleshdoom, Wielder of Shadowfang"
I have had a most disturbing experience that I must share with you, my friend. Earlier today I was called upon to help one of the men that escaped from The Labyrinth. He was deranged, violent and kept lashing out at all of those who tried to calm him. I suspected that he was possessed by some sort of demonic entity and so began to drive the evil from within him. After many hours I was able to exorcise a demon who called himself Fleshdoom, but the hellion fled into The Labyrinth. You may think that I am mad, but after speaking with the man and battling with Fleshdoom I believe that The Labyrinth has somehow become a gateway to The Underworld. As you descend deeper you may find yourself upon the doorstep of hell itself. Finally, the man who was possessed retained memories of an ancient demonblade named Shadowfang. If you find the demon Fleshdoom, beware this foul sword. While I fear the dangers below grow even greater, you must find Fleshdoom and slay him. Bring the sword to me and I can destroy it, but do not wield it for its power can corrupt absolutely.
Fleshdoom's demise is a great good to the world, yet Shadowfang remains! It must be found and destroyed! Do not attempt to use the demonblade, champion. It will corrupt and madden any mortal who wields it. I alone can end its dark evil.
Light be praised! You found the cursed demonblade! Only its destruction can ensure the safety of us all! Wait, what treachery is this? Ow! It burns! Hellfire...consuming me! You take this to the Hellforge and cast it in before ... noooo!

was added in

as a

PAGE: Vani
CATEGORIES: Characters
URL: https://diablo.fandom.com/wiki/Vani
======================================================================

Vani
Gender
Female
Race
Human
Affiliation
Nevesk
Lilith
Relatives
Unnamed child
Status
Deceased
Appearances
Diablo IV
Vani
was a resident of
Nevesk
.
Biography
Vani lived in Nevesk. A
Cathedral of Light
priest helped her give birth.
In
1336
, while attending a service at the Nevesk chapel, Lilith appeared, seducing Vani and the other villagers into following her.  While the priest urged them to resist Lilith, Vani took a Cathedral emblem and bashed him in the head.  The priest pleaded to her, reminding Vani that he'd helped deliver her child. However, Vani and the townsfolk continued to assault the priest as Lilith left. They placed the headless body in
Icehowl Ruins
, where
Iosef
later found it. Upon his arrival into Nevesk, Vani and the townsfolk druged Iosef, before Vani and
Oswen
locked him in a shed.
Vani and Oswen meet the Wanderer
Iosef rambled like a madman about
demons
and bit Oswen's hand.
The Wanderer
overheared the interaction when entering the village and investigated. Vani lied to the Wanderer, saying that Iosef had come to the village as a madman, yelling about what he had seen inside the ruins.
She asked the Wanderer to investigate the ruins.
The Wanderer succeeded, to Vani's apparent surprise. She posed a celebration with the other villagers in order to drug the Wanderer. Oswen wheeled the Wanderer away for a sacrificial ritual, but was killed by Iosef, who saved the Wanderer.
Afterwards, Vani and the other townsfolk attacked, but they were killed.
In-game
Vani is an
NPC
in
Diablo IV
. She is found in
Nevesk
. She is first introduced inside a shack with
Oswen
and
Iosef
as part of the "
Dusk on the Mountain
"
quest
. She later becomes a
monster
and is able to be killed. As a monster, she uses a
bow
.

PAGE: Vendral Trost

Gender

Vendral Trost
is an
NPC
in
Diablo IV
.
Biography
Vendral was the father of
Corik
. According to Vendral, his son killed another boy his age, and when the authorities found out what he did, he was bound in irons and taken to the
Black Asylum
, which was abandoned years later, leaving the inmates aside. However, Corik cast doubt on this account, saying that "father lied" and that Vendral had apparently never faced him directly over the circumstances of the incident.
In
1336
, Vendral was tormented by the spirit of his son, begging him to visit him in the Asylum.
The Wanderer
encountered Vendral outside
Kyovashad
, who gave his account of what had happened to Corik, and begged the Wanderer to end Corik's torment. The Wanderer entered the Black Asylum and laid Corik's spirit to rest, but when they returned to Vendral, told him that Corik loathed him. Vendral stated that he still heard Corik's cries, and alluded to a role he may have played in the murder, referring to a sin of his making, of the
blood
on his hands, and how he would never be free from the truth. Begging the
Heavens
to forgive him, he wandered off into the snow, saying that he was going to visit his son.
In-game
Vendral Trost can be found northeast of the eastern exit of
Kyovashad
. Talking to him initiates the
side quest
"
Cries of Innocence
."

"Hey! I don't need eyes to hear you passing by me!"

Biography
"What happened to your eyes?"
"Theya stole them. Pinned them on some necklace she wears, but takes it with her everywhere, makes me watch. I wonder if my suffering aids her? Ah yeah, I can see through those eyes just as you can see me now, but what I see is painful. So much pain, so much death, I want my damned eyes back!"
- The Wanderer and Vilek
(
src
)
Sometime in the 1330s, Vilek's eyes were stolen by
Theya
; a cultist of the
Triune
. However, he could still see through them. His eyes were worn in a necklace around her neck, and he was forced to watch every foul deed that she committed. He wondered if the suffering aided her in some manner.
In
1336
, Vilek was in the stocks of Kyovashad. He heard
the Wanderer
passing by, and he told them how Theya had stolen his eyes. He begged the Wanderer to retrieve them. The Wanderer noted that Vilek seemed insane, but nevertheless obliged, slaying Theya in
Nostrava
, and returned with Vilek's eyes in hand. Vilek noted that he could see himself through his own eyes, and slid them back into his sockets. However, when the eyes were slotted back in, Vilek screamed that his sockets were burning. He ran away, screaming.
In-game
Vilek is an
NPC
in
Diablo IV
. He can be found in the stocks of Kyovashad. Talking to him will initiate the
side quest
"
Sight to Madness
." Upon completion of the quest, a burning effect is applied to Vilek, though it is unclear if this is literal, or representing the 'burning' of his eyes. Somehow free of the stocks at this moment, he runs to Kyovashad's northwestern exit before disappearing.

======================================================================
PAGE: Vithu
CATEGORIES: Characters
URL: https://diablo.fandom.com/wiki/Vithu
======================================================================

Vithu
Gender
Male
Race
Human
Occupation
Artist
Status
Unknown
Appearances
Diablo Immortal
(mentioned only)
Vithu
was an artist.
Biography
When Vithu stood even a few feet off the ground, he heard his own voice urging him to jump. Once he could no longer sleep, he painted the tenebrous
Void
he saw in his dreams.
Vithu's paintings were adored throughout the provinces, and many called him a seer. Patrons chased the sublimity of his feelings. In one year, a dozen leaping
deaths
from the heights were recorded in
Fengge
.
Vithu was consumed by guilt and left Fengge, vowing to paint no more. A year later he was visited by a young girl asking for his work, with a penknife held unsteadily in her hand.
Vithu opened his door with downcast eyes, certain that she had come for revenge. He was shocked when she begged to be his apprentice.
The girl,
Miray
, confessed that she imagined the Void years ago, and drew it for her parents. If Vithu was guilty of their deaths, she was as well. But she preferred to blame the Void.
Vithu accepted Miray's apprenticeship, and they painted the Void in new colors, undeniable but robbed of all its power.
Eventually, Vithu was surpassed by his student in talent, which aroused fury in him towards her.
He painted the void in deep colors on her ceiling which immediately began to darken. By the time she returned that night he was gone, and perfectly oval holes cut through the roof and floor of her home.
In-game
Vithu is mentioned in
Diablo Immortal
in the text flavor of
Vithu's Urges
item set
.
Trivia
This section contains facts and trivia relevant to this article.
It is not clear if Vithu left after his final painting, or he was transfixed by it until the void eroded him.
References

PAGE: Wandering Trader
CATEGORIES: Characters
URL: https://diablo.fandom.com/wiki/Wandering_Trader
======================================================================

The following article contains information from  the
Diablo I
expansion
Hellfire
, which is of ambiguous canon status.
"We had a cool feature designed: a wandering trader. The initial artistic concept was a gnome-like guy with a backpack taller than he was, with pots and pans hanging off of it."
-
Donald Tsang
(src)
The "Wandering Trader"
Gender
Male
Race
Gnome
Appearances
Diablo: Hellfire
The
Wandering Trader
is a cut character planned for
Diablo: Hellfire
. He was going to be the only new salesman introduced in the
Hellfire
expansion, but he would trade itens directly rather than sell them for
gold
.
Contrary to
Celia
and
Complete Nut
, he cannot be restored through the
Command.txt exploit
since he never was fully implemented.  However, he was adapted as a new NPC in a fan mod for
Diablo
named
Belzebub
.
Design
He is not an inhabitant of
Tristram
, futhermore, his humanity is ambiguous since he was planned to look like and act like a gnome. Contrary to the other NPCs, he was going to be able to walk around Tristram and choose a spot to remain idle, thus being the only unhostile NPC able to move.
If interacted with, he would sing a ditty describing what he was looking for, the possibilities being a non-magical piece of equipment, and if the player traded with him, he'd toss them something magical in return. Every magical item given by the Wandering Trader would be as useful as the non-magical item he asked for.
Should be noted, in the original game other NPCs (
Gillian
,
Griswold
and
Ogden
) were supposed to have the ability to walk around Tristram, but it was cut for unknown reasons.

PAGE: Warlord of Blood (Monster)

For other meanings of the term, see
Warlord of Blood
.
"My blade sings for your blood, mortal. And, by my
Dark Masters
, it shall NOT be denied!"
- The Warlord of Blood
(
src
)
Warlord of Blood
Title
Executioner of Hell
Gender
Male
Race
Human
(formerly)
Demon
Affiliation
Burning Hells
Class
Steel Lord
Status
Deceased
Appearances
Diablo
The Awakening
The
Warlord of Blood
was a servant of the
Burning Hells
. Possessing great skill with the
blade
, he lived for thousands of years and knew only warfare.
Biography
"The armories of Hell are home to the Warlord of Blood. In his wake lay the mutilated bodies of thousands. Angels and Man alike have been cut down to fulfill his endless sacrifices to the Dark Ones who scream for one thing - blood."
(
src
)
It is written that the Warlord of Blood was a
human
who fought during the
Sin War
. Fighting alongside the
Legion of Darkness
, he lost his humanity due to his insatiatble lust for
blood
. He resided within the
Armories of Hell
, surrounded by the bodies of mortals and
angels
. During the
Darkening of Tristram
, he was defeated by a
trio
of
heroes
.
In-game
The Warlord of Blood is a
Unique
Steel Lord
found on
Level 13
in
Diablo
. He is found in the Armories surrounding the staircase descending to the
next level
. He spawns as part of the "
Warlord of Blood
" quest. He is accompanied by several
Steel Lords
, though because of his color swap he looks nearly like a Blood Knight.
The Warlord of Blood is immune to Fire, Lightning and most magic including
Bone Spirit
,
Blood Star
and
Flash
. Because of this, he is especially difficult for
Sorcerers
, though Sorcerers with
Stone Curse
can kill him slowly with melee attacks. It's easiest and often best for sorcerers to simply not fight him, loot the room and descend the stairs. But, one way to defeat him with a Sorcerer is cast the
Golem
spell and keep turning him to stone until the Golem kills him. The rest of the game's classes, even with the
expansion
installed, stand a chance fighting him as they would any other foe. For a melee class with low damage,
Griswold's Edge
can help by inflicting
Knockback
upon the Warlord of Blood. This can serve as a stun if nothing else, preventing him from inflicting too much damage on the player.

Trivia
This section contains facts and trivia relevant to this article.
According to
The Awakening
, the Warlord of Blood is the same individual as
Bartuc
, who also went by the title. This is contradicted in later lore however, with Bartuc being slain in the
Mage Clan Wars
, and lore after that establishing that a long period of time went between the two conflicts.

======================================================================
PAGE: Warriv
CATEGORIES: Characters
URL: https://diablo.fandom.com/wiki/Warriv
======================================================================

Warriv
Gender
Male
Race
Human
Ethnicity
Kehjistani
Occupation
Caravan master
Status
Deceased
Appearances
Diablo II
Diablo III
To Hell and Back
Warriv
was a caravan master who helped a group of heroes in their pursuit of the
Dark Wanderer
.
Biography
Early Travels
By
1264
, Warriv had been making the
Aranoch
-
Khanduras
trade route for over twenty years. He was often attacked by bandits and outlaws, but never when he had a
paladin
accompanying him. Warriv had great gratitude for the service of their
order
as a result.
During his visits to
Lut Gholein
, he met
Meshif
, a ship captain. Warriv enjoyed listening to his stories about the strange lands of the east.
Dark Wanderings
"Greetings, strangers. I am Warriv, a caravan master unable to complete my journey to the East. I'm not surprised to see your kind here. Many adventurers have traveled this way since the recent troubles began."
- Warriv greets the heroes
(
src
)
Warriv
Warriv was present in Khanduras when the
Dark Wanderer
began traveling eastward. Shortly after he passed the
Rogue Monestary
, strange creatures began ravaging the countryside, and the monastery itself was overrun. He set up shop in the
Rogue Encampment
alongside the
Sisters of the Sightless Eye
, while he waited for the eastward pass to re-open, so he could travel to Lut Gholein.
Such a thing was accomplished by a group of heroes, whom Warriv greeted at the camp. They slew
Andariel
, and with her death, the path to the east opened. Warriv took them along with his caravan as they traveled east, along with the scholar
Deckard Cain
,
whom Warriv considered to be a madman.
The group arrived in Lut Gholein after a dangerous journey across the desert. Warriv was shocked at the state of the port-city, noting the presence of mercenaries.
He decided that once he made some trades, he would return and give equipment to the Sisterhood. He offered the heroes the chance to return with him if they so desired. As the case was however, they were forced to keep traveling east, as the Dark Wanderer had beaten them to the
Tomb of Tal Rasha
and was traveling eastward with
Baal
. Warriv suspected that they were headed for
Kurast
, and was confident the heroes would succeed.
Warriv's End
"I return to Khanduras after twenty years, the burden of countless failures and tragedies heaped upon my shoulders. Am I being punished for helping that stranger hunt the Dark Wanderer? I always thought Deckard Cain half a madman, but perhaps...he was right. Perhaps he can banish the shadow hanging over my life."
- Warriv
(
src
)
Warriv's body
The following decades were not kind on Warriv, as he suffered numerous failures and tragedies. After twenty years, he returned to Khanduras, wondering if Cain hadn't been the madman he thought, and if he could banish the shadow that dwelt over him.
He did not live long enough to find out, as he was killed outside
New Tristram
.
In-game
Diablo II
Warriv
Act I
Act II
Appears in
Diablo II
Significance
Medium
Service(s)
gossip, travelling between
Act I
and
Act II
Residence(s)
Rogue Encampment
,
Lut Gholein
Starts quest(s)
None
Portrayed by
Michael McConnohie
Warriv is the first character encountered at the start of a new game in
Diablo II
. He greets the player and explains the current state of the
Rogue Encampment
. After the death of
Andariel
, he invites the heroes who slew her to join his caravan and travel on to
Lut Gholein
through the
Rogue Pass
. His outfit changes between acts—the only NPC in the game where this occurs.
Dialogue
Main article:
Warriv/Dialogue
Diablo III
Although this does not happen in every game, his corpse can sometimes be found in
Act I
of
Diablo III
. It will be located among the remains of his caravan a short way up
Old Tristram Road
out of town, and can be looted to find his
journal
.
Personality and Traits
"Warriv's advice is like corpse gas; it befouls the air for a moment and then disapears."
—
Gheed
Warriv was a dour adage-sayer,
and a large man with a stern demeanor.
He was skeptical of rumors of treasure.
Still, he always had a smile for those who visited the Rogue Encampment.
Trivia
This section contains facts and trivia relevant to this article.
Warriv and the
Necromancer
are both voiced by
Michael McConnohie
, who is also known for his roles as
Kel'Thuzad
and
Uther the Lightbringer
in the
Warcraft
series.

Biography
During the reign of King
Fahir
, Watep was one of 1000 individuals sacrificed inside the
Chamber of Wisdom
for the sake of their king. His body lay slumped against a wall inside the chamber.
Centuries (if not millennia) later, Watep rose from the
dead
to attack a
hero/group of heroes
who had entered the chamber. However, Watep was again slain.
In-game

during the

"
Wisdom's Fragment
". His body reanimates when the "Search for Lingering
Souls
" stage of the quest triggers.
Watep is immune to
knockback
, and can lob an arc of
fireballs
at the player. There is a brief AoE marker indicating where they will land. Additionally, there is a laser-beam attack, going around in a 360 arc. He is assisted by regular Skull Cleavers during the fight.

Willa's in-game portrait
Willa Rathe
is a
ghost
NPC
, always found in the
Decaying Crypt
Level 2 in
Diablo III
.
In life, she was the daughter of
Father Rathe
and
Mother Rathe
, as well as the elder sister of
Little Jebby Rathe
.
When found, Willa is crying over the madness that consumed her family in their unlife, and upon talking to her, say she can hear them digging without end. She will then beg
the Nephalem
to release the Rathes from their torment. If a
follower
is present, they will say that Willa is telling the truth. This will initiate
The Family of Rathe
event
.
Killing all three family members will allow Willa to be at peace as well.

PAGE: Wirt
CATEGORIES: Characters
URL: https://diablo.fandom.com/wiki/Wirt
======================================================================

"Pssst...over here..."
- Wirt greeting a hero
(
src
)
Wirt
Title
The Peg-Legged Boy
Gender
Male
Affiliation
Himself
Relatives
Canace
(mother)
Status
Deceased
Appearances
Diablo
Diablo: Hellfire
Diablo II
The Awakening
Book of Cain
Wirt the Peg-Legged Boy
was a youth from
Tristram
. During the time of
Diablo
's awakening, he offered his services to heroes as a smuggler/peddler.
Biography
The Darkening of Tristram
"Poor Wirt. I did all that was possible for the child, but I know he despises that wooden peg that I was forced to attach to his leg. His wounds were hideous. No one - and especially such a young child - should have to suffer the way he did."
-
Pepin
on Wirt
(
src
)
Wirt grew up in
Tristram
and had a knack for getting into trouble. He also had a knack for shady dealings, ranging from simple sign stealing to setting up connections with guilds outside town. However, his troubles were compounded along with the rest of the townspeople when a darkness settled over King
Leoric
, the result of Diablo's corruption. Events reached a head when
Fallen Ones
raided the town, kidnapping a number of children. Wirt was among them, torn from the arms of his
mother
. Down in the depths of the
Tristram Cathedral
, Wirt and the children were tortured by the
demons
.
Griswold
saved Wirt and returned him to Tristram.
Pepin
the Healer did what he could for the boy, but while Wirt's life was saved, his left leg wasn't. The events led to a change in Wirt's personality, a darkness hanging over him. His mother died soon after his rescue—from a broken heart, according to
Gillian
. Griswold offered Wirt a job at his smithy, but Wirt refused—his plans were to make
gold
, get out of Tristram and hopefully take Gillian with him, whom he had a crush on
(not that she was aware of it).
Still, in the meantime, he was willing to work as a stable boy in the
Tavern of the Rising Sun
, being polite to those who needed their horses stabled...and privately accosting adventurers to sell them his stolen merchandise.
Of Business and Butchery
Wirt in Tristram
After the incident, Wirt became delusional, believing Tristram has no hope for salvation. Given his condition, he has no chance but to stay in town. By striking secretive dealings with urchins and unspoken guilds of nearby towns, Wirt was able to gain access to all sorts of distinct goods that couldn't be found so easily in Tristram. He then starts to slowly build a small fortune from the many adventurers heroes that were drawn to Tristram, hearing news of the evil said to lurk beneath the cathedral. This suited Wirt just fine by selling his goods to them
, and planned to use this money to leave town. Eventually, a trio of heroes led by
Aidan
,
King Leoric
's son, felled Diablo and an uneasy peace returned to Tristram.
After a period of time, Aidan, who had been corrupted by Diablo after inserting the
soulstone
on his head in the hopes of containing the Lord of Terror, suddenly left, and demons descended upon the townsfolk. With no able bodied warriors present, the result was a bloodbath.
Wirt was among those killed—the first victim of rampaging
Hell Bovines
.
His body was later found by a new group of heroes.
In-game
Diablo
Wirt in Diablo
Wirt appears as an
NPC
in
Diablo
. He does not initiate any quests, but he sells items to the player. However, his method differs from other NPCs in that the player has to pay 50 gold pieces to see what item he's selling, not to mention that Wirt only sells one item at a time. This was the first form of
gambling
in the Diablo franchise, although the mechanics differ from later iterations.
Quotes
Not everyone in Tristram has a use - or a market - for everything you will find in the labyrinth. Not even me, as hard as that is to believe. Sometimes, only you will be able to find a purpose for some things.
Don't trust everything the
drunk
says. Too many ales have fogged his vision and his good sense.
In case you haven't noticed, I don't buy anything from Tristram. I am an importer of quality goods. If you want to peddle junk, you'll have to see Griswold, Pepin or that witch,
Adria
. I'm sure that they will snap up whatever you can bring them...
I guess I owe the blacksmith my life - what there is of it. Sure, Griswold offered me an apprenticeship at the smithy, and he is a nice enough guy, but I'll never get enough money to... well, let's just say that I have definite plans that require a large amount of gold.
If I were a few years older, I would shower her with whatever riches I could muster, and let me assure you I can get my hands on some very nice stuff. Gillian is a beautiful girl who should get out of Tristram as soon as it is safe. Hmmm... maybe I'll take her with me when I go...
Cain
knows too much. He scares the life out of me - even more than that woman across the river. He keeps telling me about how lucky I am to be alive, and how my story is foretold in legend. I think he's off his crock.
Farnham - now there is a man with serious problems, and I know all about how serious problems can be. He trusted too much in the integrity of one man, and Lazarus led him into the very jaws of death. Oh, I know what it's like down there, so don't even start telling me about your plans to destroy the evil that dwells in that Labyrinth. Just watch your legs...
As long as you don't need anything reattached, old Pepin is as good as they come. If I'd have had some of those potions he brews, I might still have my leg...
Adria truly bothers me. Sure, Cain is creepy in what he can tell you about the past, but that witch can see into your past. She always has some way to get whatever she needs, too. Adria gets her hands on more merchandise than I've seen pass through the gates of the King's Bazaar during High Festival.
Ogden
is a fool for staying here. I could get him out of town for a very reasonable price, but he insists on trying to make a go of it with that stupid tavern. I guess at the least he gives Gillian a place to work, and his wife
Garda
does make a superb Shepherd's pie...
Diablo II
Wirt's body, as found in
Diablo II
In
Diablo II
, Wirt's corpse lies among the ruins of
Tristram
. His is the only corpse identified by name; with the exception of
Deckard Cain
, the rest of the town's familiar faces are either missing, assumed to be dead from skeletons where they once stood, or
worse
. His body contains a lot of gold and
his leg
, one of the objects required to open the
Secret Cow Level
.
When Wirt's corpse is clicked his gold doesn't drop to the ground all at once as normal, but individual piles "rain down" around his corpse. This "shower of gold" is probably a reference to Wirt's vendor function in the previous game, as he used to ask for a lot of money just so players could "take a peek" at his items.
Diablo III
In
Diablo III
,
Wirt's Original Leg
drops from the corpse of
Bishibosh
(
Act I
,
The Weeping Hollow
Den of the Fallen
Level 2). There is also an item called
Wirt's Bell
which is needed to access
Whimsyshire
. Another item called
Wirt's Leg
which is required to complete a semi-secret side quest in
The Darkening of Tristram
(event).
In Other Games
In
Hellgate: London
(which was developed by ex-
Blizzard North
veterans) exists a quest reward named "Wart's Peg Leg", which seems to be a parody of "Wirt's Leg".
Warcraft
In
Warcraft III: The Frozen Throne
, there is an item called
Wirt's Other Leg
that can be found in a level in the blood elf campaign. The item is, quite coincidentally, found behind an abomination called
the Butcher
. The item has no properties in the game, except for this flavor text:
"Perhaps the overzealous adventurer pried this off before his journey here thinking it might give him one last opportunity at
bovine slaughter
. Little did he know where it would lead him."
In
World of Warcraft
, there is another item called
Wirt's Third Leg
.
As part of the "A Greedy Emissary" world event,
Wirt's Fightin' Leg
,
Wirt's Haunted Leg
, and
Wirt's Last Leg
can be obtained. The flavor text of each item reads
"Who's Wirt?"
Personality and Traits
"Wirt is a rapscallion and a little scoundrel. He was always getting into trouble, and it's no surprise what happened to him. He probably went fooling about someplace that he shouldn't have been. I feel sorry for the boy, but I don't abide the company that he keeps."
-
Ogden
(
src
)
While Wirt was a "rapscallion and a scoundrel" before the loss of his leg, the ordeal cast a darkness over his soul. The boy became cold, pragmatic and delusional, believing Tristram was beyond salvation and that the only path was fleeing the cursed town; something he had in plan once he amassed his fortune.
Most of townsfolk of Tristram were sympathetic to Wirt's condition.
Pepin
in particular lamented the situation, as he was the one who mended the boy's wounds and attached the wooden peg to his leg; the town healer stated that no one, especially a child, should suffer the way Wirt did.
Gillian
was the most kind towards the boy, but was also unaware of his feelings for her.
The boy's connections and methods to acquire goods of dubious origins were well known among the town.
Griswold
worried for the boy and hoped he would instead take honest work rather than those shady dealings.
Ogden
disapproved Wirt's actions and the company he kept, referring to the merchants and urchins who would come to Tristram, and part of the source of the's boy acquired goods.
When interacting with heroes, Wirt demonstrated a sarcastic, profit-driven mindset—dismissive of his fellow villagers and just as dismissive of the hero's efforts.
He focused entirely on himself, and what he could steal.
His heart was further darkened by Gillian being blind to his affections.
Trivia
This section contains facts and trivia relevant to this article.
Wirt's peg leg stems from what was seen as an unfixable bug which caused Wirt to walk with a slight limp. Frustrated,
Eric Flannum
ripped Wirt's leg off and gave him a peg one to account for the limp.
During the development of
Diablo
, Wirt's sanity was in decay due to his trauma after losing his leg. The boy would have lapses and start talking backwards in riddles. This was ultimately cut from the final game, but lines of Wirt talking backwards related to the original version of
The Butcher
's
quest
still exist in the game's internal files.
Wirt's name rhymes with
Squirt
, the vendor who sells
Wirt's Bell
in
Diablo III
.
Wirt's spirit is featured as the main antagonist in the Critical Role's
Diablo
oneshot
, obsessed with gathering gold for Gillian.

Woodruh, Forsaken Warden
, is a
Transformed
boss
seen in
Diablo Immortal
.
Biography
Woodruh was once the warden of the
prison
beneath
Stormpoint Keep
. Despite his grim role, he was a friendly person.
Transformed
"Thought it was just an ordinary rock. Nice deep crimson, decent shine on it. Put it on the bedstand; next day, I passed around the mess. One of the green guards gets a real long look, makes for to grab it, next he's spewing seawater and his face is splitting open like a crab. Meris had to kill him with a fire poker. Every hair's on my back is falling out, and my skin's going to go next. Hell of a week."
- Woodruh in his
journal
(
src
)
One day, he found a
red rock
in the
tidal cave
beneath his office. Taking it as an ordinary rock, he put it on his bedstand. The next day, he passed it around the mess to see if any of the guards could identify it. A rookie guard reached to grab it for a closer inspection. Next thing, the guard started vomiting seawater, and his body began twisting to a monstrous form.
Another guard
had to put the rookie down, using a fire poker.
Later, Woodruh noticed that his hairs began falling out. Seeing as the transformation was affecting most of the residents, both prisoner and jailor alike, he arranged for the prisoners with lighter crimes who had not started transforming to be moved to
the Shanties
. The hardened criminals who were "monsters in human skin" remained locked up.
When it was clear that reinforcements from
Westmarch
were not coming, he ordered
Commander Kenton
to seal the prison. As he was already changing, he decided to stay in the prison to make sure none of the monsters make it out.
Even as the changes ravaged his body, he managed to retain parts of his mind, and still made patrols around the prison. One day, he befriended a sea creature he found in the cave. With his mental faculties already warped, he decided to share "
his Heart
" with the creature.
As a result, the creature started to transform over time, eventually growing into a
behemoth
. One day, it stole the shard and swallowed it. By now Woodruh was a shadow of his former self, and was obsessed with the shard. The despair of losing the shard proved to be the final straw for his mind.
Bound for Eternity
"Where is it? Still hear it beat. Warm like the lash. Cold like fire to the fingertips. Mine."
- Woodruh's last journal entry
(
src
)
Trapped in the prison and with close proximity to the Worldstone, he continued to painfully warp and warp; constantly clawing at himself in pain and despair. Even when confronted by
the Shard-seeker
, he continued to mutate.
This section is a
stub
. You can help the Diablo Wiki to become more awesome by
expanding it
.
In-game
"
It
is mine it is mine, mine, mine!"
- Woodruh
(
src
)
Dialogue box portrait of a heavily mutated Woodruh
The Warden is a
monster
in
Diablo Immortal
. He is fought as a
boss
in the
Abandoned Prison
in the
storyline quest
"
Bound for Eternity
."
Trivia
This section contains facts and trivia relevant to this article.
The Warden is a sort of 'inverse character' in
Diablo Immortal
. Up to the events of
Terror's Tide
, the Worldstone shards in the game were routinely used by evil individuals. The Warden is meant to show what happens when the Worldstone "has its way with a place and a people."
After losing his mind, Woodruh's character is similar to the
Gollum
from
Lord of the Rings
.

in

.
The Wretched Queen has to be killed in the quest
The Fallen Star
, being, in fact, the first Super-Unique monster encountered in game. She has far more health than the average Mother, and higher damage. She also has unique appearance, with white bloodied dress and pale hair (as opposed to black-haired regular Wretched Mothers).

History
The trade of
Dawning Echo
for Platinum was added in the
Nightmare Manifest
update.
Ancient Scrap, and therefore the ability to exchange Ancient Artifacts for it, was introduced in the
September 10, 2025
update. Previously, lower-tier Ancient Artifacts would sit uselessly in the player's inventory.
Originally, there were every single difficulty, with corresponding exchange options at the Smithing Materials Vendor. In the
December 17, 2025
update, all Fabled Wisps below Inferno VII were converted into an item that is just called "Fable Wisp", while those from Inferno VII onwards retained their tiers.

======================================================================
PAGE: Zorun Tzin
CATEGORIES: Characters
URL: https://diablo.fandom.com/wiki/Zorun_Tzin
======================================================================

Zorun Tzin
was a powerful spellcaster who lived in the eastern empire of
Kehjan
during the early days of
Sanctuary
. He appears in the third of
Richard A. Knaak
's
Sin War
novels,
The Veiled Prophet
.
Background
Zorun Tzin was the second son of the famous mage
Liov Tzin
. Zorun Tzin was described as being a gaunt, bearded and dark-skinned mage with thinning grey hair. Zorun Tzin had been contracted by the
Council of Clans
to discover more about the
Edyrem
and their mysterious power. Zorun regularly tortured prisoners by magical means in order to extract information, and he did not hesitate to take lives. In secret, Zorun hoped to capture the Edyrem's leader,
Uldyssian
, in order to harness his unbridled powers. Zorun also had an assistant, the giant
Terul
.
It bothered Zorun that the Edyrem - who he scornfully called 'peasants'- possessed tremendous powers, while it had required him a lifetime of intense studying in order to acquire his spell-casting skills. This was also one of Zorun's flaws - one that ultimately proved to be fatal: his ego.
Through magical means, Zorun ambushed Uldyssian as he was travelling along with Master
Fahin
's caravan. Fahin and all of the caravan's guard were slain in the process. Zorun then turned on his own bodyguards who were send by the Mage Clans to both guard and monitor their agent, killing them as well.
Uldysssian was taken to Zorun's sanctum for interrogation. However, while Zorun was distracted by emissaries of the Mage Clans, his servant Terul - who was in fact possessed by
Malic
- tried to possess Uldyssian. Uldyssian managed to escape his predicament, blasting Zorun's chamber and incinerating Terul. As Zorun rushed into the chamber, Malic's vile spirit possessed him, killing the mage.
Zorun's body was later disposed of in the tunnels beneath Kehjan, as Malic's spirit found a new host to inhabit. Zorun's body was fed to a ravenous water demon, destroying any remaining traces of the mage.
This article is a
stub
. You can help the Diablo Wiki to become more awesome by
expanding it
.
